Rural Life Series

Purpose of Publication 36

— Edited by Yu Qing-tang of the China Social Education Society — Yu Qing-tang

The severity of China's rural problems and the hardship of farmers' lives have now reached their extreme. Who is not alarmed by the fact that years of droughts and floods have wiped out the lives and property of so many people; the recent Yellow River disaster has left more than 300,000 victims in western Shandong homeless, and more than one million victims in northern Jiangsu are drifting and waiting to die? Who does not know that during times of disaster, there is naturally no harvest, and even in good years, the dumping of foreign agricultural products causes the prices of domestic agricultural products to fall below the cost? And who has not heard of the gradual decrease in cultivated land, the rapid increase in poor and tenant farmers, the destruction of rural handicrafts, and the decline of national new industries, making it impossible for healthy farmers to use their labor? More than 300 million poor and helpless farmers are living inhuman, oppressed lives under the threat of the world economy and the shackles of old production relations!

How to cope with the threat of the world economic system without being hit by it, and how to transform the old production relations and be liberated from its shackles, so that farmers can first recuperate and then freely develop their productive forces and live a rational social life? This is the real issue of the current rural problem.

The purpose of this column is to: (1) provide the actual situation of rural areas in various provinces and regions, and depict the real suffering of the rural people; (2) dissect the role and influence of foreign economic forces in rural areas; (3) analyze and compare the latest rural economic statistical materials to show the real situation of rural decline; (4) introduce farmers' opinions on their own joys and sorrows in life and on the current situation; (5) introduce theories on improving rural life at home and abroad, as well as successful experimental undertakings. If these materials can arouse our vigilance, thinking, verification, and research, and enable the rural problem to have a reasonable solution, then this small column will have fulfilled its possible task.

The drafts published in this column pay special attention to the following standards: First, the content is original, the length is not very long, but it is a perspective and writing of folk life, not any existing material without thinking. Second, the text is interesting, lively and lively. Third, the realism must be timely, such as the recent attacks on rural areas by disasters and soldiers, and we will do our best to introduce them to arouse everyone's enthusiasm and efforts for relief. Fourth, the materials should be representative in terms of geographic area, and should be as comprehensive as possible, without being limited to any corner of the country.

We sincerely contribute this column to the readers, hoping that our vast readership, especially those who live in rural areas and those who are engaged in practical rural work, can regularly provide us with valuable materials. The gradual creation of public opinion; the gradual accumulation of objective materials: the gradual clarification of the real nature of rural problems; from the disclosure of practical work to the discussion and resolution of problems: all of this depends on the collective strength of the people of the whole country, and it is what we deeply expect.

A Few Opinions on the Land Rent Problem 37

— Bai Liang

In recent years, China's rural areas have been in constant turmoil. There are many reasons for this, but the land rent problem is indeed a major one. Therefore, if we want to stabilize the rural areas, in addition to abolishing the private ownership of land and fundamentally abolishing land rent, we must at least find a proper solution to the land rent problem before it can be effective. Otherwise, even if we try to maintain stability for the time being, it will be difficult to avoid long-term turmoil. I am not talented, but I would like to contribute some opinions on the land rent rate in the "Rural Life" section for everyone's reference.

The high land rent in China, whether in kind or in cash, is very obvious; for example, rent in kind often accounts for more than 50% of the output, and rent in cash often accounts for more than 10% of the land price. Therefore, China's "purchase year" is shorter than that of other countries. Therefore, some people say that China's land rent is not only land rent, but also includes a part of agricultural dividends and even a part of wages. Because the land rent is too high, tenant farmers cannot afford it, so there has been a rent reduction movement in recent years. For example, the "25% Rent Reduction Method" proposed by the Kuomintang in the 15th year of the Republic of China is one example. This method is to reduce 25% of the original rent amount, regardless of the amount of the original rent, so it is called "25% Rent Reduction." However, since this rent reduction method was proposed, it has only been implemented once in Zhejiang Province, and has not been effectively implemented in other regions. Even if it has been implemented occasionally, it has only caused disputes, leading to a rent reduction movement that is nominal rather than real, or a rent reduction movement that disrupts the rural areas. The reason for this is that, in addition to landlords opposing rent reduction and the government not effectively enforcing the law, there are also problems with the "25% Rent Reduction" itself. First, the meaning of "25% Rent Reduction" is unclear. Some people interpret it as first deducting 25% from the total harvest of agricultural crops as compensation for the capital invested by the tenant farmer (all by-products belong to the tenant farmer), and the remaining 75% is divided equally between the landlord and the tenant farmer, that is, each gets 37.5%. In other words, the landlord gets 37.5% and the tenant farmer gets 62.5%. This is the meaning of deducting 25% from the total amount of production. Others interpret it as first dividing the harvest equally, that is, the landlord and tenant each get half, and then deducting 25% from the rent paid by the tenant to the landlord. In this way, the landlord only gets 25% and the tenant farmer can get 75%. This is the so-called deducting 25% from the rent agreement or deducting 25% from the agreed rent amount. Since there are two different interpretations of "25% Rent Reduction," if the landlord's income was originally above 50%, he will definitely agree with the first interpretation and adopt the former method of rent reduction, while the tenant farmer will agree with the second interpretation and adopt the latter method of rent reduction. Conversely, if the landlord's income was originally below 50%, he will agree with the second interpretation and adopt the latter method of rent reduction, while the tenant farmer will inevitably agree with the first interpretation and adopt the former method of rent reduction. Because of the different interpretations, many disputes arise between landlords and tenants, and as a result, "25% Rent Reduction" becomes even more difficult to implement. Second, even if there are no interpretive disputes in "25% Rent Reduction," and no disputes arise between landlords and tenants, and the "25% Rent Reduction" method is implemented, unfair phenomena will inevitably occur for both landlords and tenants due to the different grades of land and the different yields. For example, after various counties in Zhejiang implemented the 25% rent reduction standard (with 37.5% as the rent amount), the income of tenant farmers and landlords was still not balanced, as shown in the following example:

Total Harvest per Mu Tenant Farmer's Income Production Cost Tenant Farmer's Net Income Landlord's Income Taxes Paid by Landlord Landlord's Net Income

3 Shi 18.75 yuan 6.00 yuan 12.75 yuan 11.15 yuan 1.00 yuan 10.25 yuan

2 Shi 5 Dou 15.63 yuan 6.00 yuan 9.63 yuan 9.37 yuan 1.00 yuan 8.37 yuan

2 Shi 13.50 yuan 6.00 yuan 7.50 yuan 7.50 yuan 1.00 yuan 6.50 yuan

1 Shi 5 Dou 9.38 yuan 6.00 yuan 3.38 yuan 5.62 yuan 1.00 yuan 4.62 yuan

1 Shi 6.15 yuan 6.00 yuan 0.15 yuan 3.75 yuan 1.00 yuan 2.75 yuan

5 Dou 3.13 yuan 6.00 yuan -2.87 yuan 1.87 yuan 1.00 yuan 0.87 yuan

From the above table, it can be seen that after the implementation of "25% Rent Reduction," the net income of tenant farmers who harvest more than 2 Shi per mu is slightly more than that of landlords; for those who harvest 2 Shi per mu, the net income of landlords and tenants is equal; if the harvest is less than 2 Shi per mu, the net income of tenant farmers is far less than that of landlords, and they may even lose money. This is a very obvious display of unfairness, which is also a major reason why disputes cannot be implemented.

Since "25% Rent Reduction" has many obstacles and difficulties, the evolution of "25% Rent Reduction" has also led to the method of stipulating the highest rent amount in order to protect tenant farmers. For example, Article 2 of the Provisional Measures for Amending the 25% Rent Reduction in Zhejiang Province states: "After the promulgation of these Measures, for all newly established tenancy contracts, the rent payment amount shall be based on 37.5% of the total harvest of the normal annual production of the land, and all by-products shall belong to the tenant farmer." The National Government's Land Law Article 177 later promulgated also stipulated: "Land rent shall not exceed 375 per thousand of the total harvest of normal agricultural products. If the agreed land rent exceeds 375 per thousand, it shall be reduced to 375 per thousand. If it is less than 375 per thousand, it shall be based on the agreement." This is roughly the same, meaning to limit the highest rent amount. Although this provision can remedy the shortcomings of "25% Rent Reduction" (such as reducing 25% from the original rent amount across the board, the original high rent amount is still high, and the original low rent amount is too low, which is not fair), it also has inappropriate points. Because land rent has differential rent (Ricardo) and absolute rent (Marx): the former is caused by the difference in land productivity, and land rent will naturally not be equal; the latter is generated by the private ownership of land, and under the private ownership of land, land rent has no difference. Since the legislative intention of the Land Law is to protect tenant farmers, its provision that the highest rent amount shall not exceed 375 per thousand can only protect wealthy tenant farmers who cultivate fertile land; while poor tenant farmers who cultivate barren land often cannot enjoy the benefits of legal protection. Because the level of land rent in China does not necessarily follow the fertility of the land, in fact, the rent rate of high-grade land is often lower than the rent rate of low-grade land. If the Land Law is implemented, the rent reduction for fertile land will be more, and the rent reduction for barren land will be less. According to recent surveys, poor tenant farmers mostly cultivate barren land. Therefore, the legal benefits stipulated by the Land Law are still not enjoyed fairly.

Another level is that if the provisions of the Land Law are to reduce and exempt the exploitation from the private ownership of land, then poor tenant farmers who cultivate barren land should be even more protected and should have their rent reduced. Because there is very little room for differential rent for those who cultivate barren land, and the land rent they pay is almost entirely the result of their blood and sweat. Under the private ownership system of land, even if it cannot be absolutely abolished, it should at least be reduced to the minimum limit to be fair. However, according to the provisions of the Land Law, this point has no effect, and it is no wonder that it is dissatisfied by the general scholars.

In addition, the Land Law stipulates that the highest rent amount shall not exceed 375 per thousand, which is sometimes enough to hinder the development of land productivity. Because the rent amount cannot exceed 375 per thousand, the landlord will naturally be unwilling to invest more capital to improve the land, and the tenant farmer is limited by his financial resources. As a result, land productivity will inevitably be restricted.

Based on the above simple description, since "25% Rent Reduction" has many obstacles and difficulties, and the provisions of the Land Law are mostly dissatisfied by scholars, then how should appropriate rent rates be stipulated under the current land private ownership system in China? The author believes that the strengths of "25% Rent Reduction" and the Land Law should be adopted. First, the land administration agency or other agencies should divide the land into three grades (or more), and then stipulate the highest rent amount separately according to the grades of land. The tenant farmer will pay the land rent according to the rent rate of each grade of land, and the landlord shall not collect land rent exceeding the rent rate of each grade of land. After that, if the landlord is willing to invest in improving the land, the grade of the land will change, and the rent rate can also be increased accordingly. Conversely, if the land reduces its productivity due to force majeure, the tenant farmer can also apply to the land administration agency or other agencies to lower the grade of the land and reduce the rent rate. For example:

The highest rent amount for high-grade land shall not exceed 375 per thousand of the total harvest of normal agricultural products; if it is less than this amount, it shall be based on the agreement.

The highest rent amount for medium-grade land shall not exceed 350 per thousand of the total harvest of normal agricultural products; if it is less than this amount, it shall be based on the agreement.

The highest rent amount for low-grade land shall not exceed 300 per thousand of the total harvest of normal agricultural products; if it is less than this amount, it shall be based on the agreement.

If there are more grades of land, the highest rent amount will also be subdivided accordingly. According to this provision, the highest rent amount can prevent landlords from collecting excessive land rent, and the highest rent amount is also differential, which is determined according to the difference in land productivity. It can take into account various tenant farmers and various land productivity, and it is much more appropriate than the provisions of the Land Law. At a time when land rent is excessively high and tenant farmers are extremely poor, it is worthy of attention by friends who are improving rural life.

National Pardon Decree for Four Offenders 38

(Nanjing) The National Government issued a decree on the 1st. The Judicial Yuan presented a report from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, which in turn received reports from the chief prosecutors of the high courts of Hebei, Shandong, and Jiangxi provinces. The reports concerned prisoners: Luo Zhao-shi, who was sentenced to life imprisonment in August of the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929) for premeditated murder; Wei Zhi-gao, who was sentenced to life imprisonment for murder and robbery; Xu Xiao-he, who was sentenced to life imprisonment for premeditated murder; and Xu Cai-yun, who was sentenced to life imprisonment in April of the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932) for premeditated murder. However, it was found that the age of each of the offenders at the time of the crime was under eighteen years old. According to Article 5 of the New Criminal Law Implementation Act, a request was made to grant a reduced sentence. Now, in accordance with Article 68 of the Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage of the Republic of China, it is declared that the life sentence originally imposed on the offender Wei Zhi-gao is reduced to a fixed term of imprisonment of twelve years. The life sentences originally imposed on the three offenders Luo Zhao-shi, Xu Xiao-he, and Xu Cai-yun are each reduced to a fixed term of imprisonment of ten years, in order to show compassion. This decree is issued. (1st, Central News Agency dispatch)

Jiangsu Relief Association Sends Telegram to Economic Commission, Requesting Expedited Closure of Breaches in Shandong Province 60

(Zhenjiang) The Provincial Relief Association telegraphed the National Economic Commission, stating that the breaches in Shandong Province had brought disaster to northern Jiangsu. Even now, while other provinces have passed the worst period, the people of Jiangsu continue to suffer an even more dire situation. Despite various efforts to relieve the crisis, the breaches upstream have not been closed, and the water flows downward. For the Huaihai region of Jiangsu Province, it is no different than holding a container under an axe's downward swing. Contemplating the future, one cannot help but feel fear and dread. Moreover, several months have passed since the river breaches occurred. The association has repeatedly telegraphed the commission, earnestly requesting that orders be given to expedite the closure of the breaches. The commission has duly relayed the orders. Now that the time of frost and receding water has arrived, there has been no news of construction beginning. If days continue to be wasted and delayed, it is sincerely feared that the work will not be completed before the peach blossoms flood again. It seems inevitable that the entire northern Jiangsu will be plunged into a state of submersion. With compassion for these disaster-stricken people, as if feeling their pain oneself, it is earnestly requested that a strict order be issued to urge and set a deadline for the start of construction to close the breaches and alleviate the crisis in Jiangsu. (1st, Special dispatch)

Beining Railway Bureau Constructs Yuguan Station 61

Simultaneous Construction of General Bureau Official Residences Makes Inter-Railway Transport Inside and Outside the Pass Difficult to Implement

Dalian Communication: The Beining Railway Bureau has recently submitted a request to the Ministry of Railways for approval to undertake two major construction projects. One is the renovation of the Shanhaiguan Station, and the other is the construction of additional official residences for the Tianjin General Bureau. Since the implementation of through train services inside and outside the Pass and the borrowing of Shanhaiguan Station by the puppet Fengshan Railway as its terminal, the local switches, ticket offices, telegraph offices, and telephone rooms have all felt cramped. Every time vehicles are exchanged or passengers transfer trains, the small size of the platform makes it extremely crowded. In addition to parking trains, there are almost no exchange tracks in the various switches. Zhu previously planned to spend money under the name of the puppet Fengshan Railway to build a new Shanhaiguan Station. The Beining Railway Bureau, however, believed that Shanhaiguan was under the jurisdiction of the bureau and that the puppet Fengshan Railway was merely borrowing the station for parking purposes. It absolutely would not allow it to usurp the role of the host. Therefore, the Engineering and Transportation Departments planned to allocate 300,000 yuan from the bureau's income to first expand essential works such as switches, bridges, dry bridges, ticket offices, and platforms. The request to the Ministry of Railways for approval to build was submitted last week. The bureau's engineers are designing, gathering labor and materials within this year, and starting construction in early spring next year. As for the second phase of construction, such as road signs and water towers, it will be started when income is slightly more abundant next year. In Tianjin, the office of the Railway Bureau's official residence, due to the increasing number of personnel and the increase in staff in various departments, is quite cramped. The most important departments of the bureau, such as the Engineering and Mechanical Departments, are located outside the bureau, and communication is often inconvenient. There is a piece of land west of the general bureau address. In addition to allocating a corner for the bureau's hospital and building a large building recently, there is still much vacant land. Therefore, the bureau specifically requested the Ministry of Railways to allow the allocation of 300,000 yuan from the road's revenue to build a new official residence. The new house is slightly larger than the old official residence, and the vaults are built in the basement. Construction has begun and is expected to be completed in June or July next year. In the future, the new and old bureaus will be connected as one, and the director's office, the General Affairs Office, and the Accounting Department will be moved in. The Engineering and Mechanical Departments will then move into the old official residence.

The matter of inter-railway transport between the Beining Railway and outside the Pass was previously rumored to be discussed in Beiping. According to a person in charge of the Beining Railway Bureau, the proposal for this matter was made by Yin Tongfu at the International Transport Conference convened in Tokyo, Japan, this spring. At that time, the Japanese side made some suggestions, but they were not included in the formal agenda. Later, although the Eastern Travel Agency convened a meeting between the parties concerned, due to the different freight rates inside and outside the Pass and the different levels of tariffs, both parties adopted a strict inspection policy for inbound and outbound goods. In fact, it is difficult to achieve inter-railway transport. Recently, Manchukuo Railway dispatched Director Ishimoto Kenji to be stationed in Tianjin, who also mentioned this matter. However, because there are still difficulties, it was shelved before formal consultation. Therefore, the rumors that the Beining Railway Bureau sent representatives, the manager of the Eastern Travel Agency Zhang Shuihong, and the Manchukuo Railway representative Ishimoto to discuss in Beiping are all untrue. As for the business situation of the Beining Railway Bureau this year, as of now, it is not good. It has decreased by more than half compared to last year. This is due to the small number of passengers and the stagnation of freight transport to Australia. Among them, the slow sales of Kailuan coal have had the greatest impact on the road's revenue. Recently, Kailuan, in order to dump its coal, discussed with the Railway Bureau a method of reducing freight rates, which will be implemented soon. The fee reduction contract will be cancelled and the original contract will be restored if Kailuan's business is prosperous and the coal sales reach a considerable number.

Public Prostitution District Established Outside Changmen 63

Since the prohibition of prostitution in our city in the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927), the Minsheng Singing Club was established on the Changmen Road, which was a transformation of the long-term book house group secretly engaging in prostitution. Private prostitutes filling various hostels are a particularly prominent phenomenon. Now, the Public Security Bureau has adopted the provincial capital's method of establishing a public prostitution district, which will be implemented immediately. Minqingli is designated as first-class (the old site of the long-term book house), Tongchunfang, etc. as second-class (same as above), and Lerongfang as third-class (the old site of the yo-er brothel). The flower nameplate lights are red with gold lettering for first-class, red with blue lettering for second-class, and red with white lettering for third-class. The accommodation fee is ten yuan for first-class, seven yuan for second-class, and five yuan for third-class. Detailed regulations such as inspection methods have also been formulated. Registration began on the 1st.

Incoming Correspondence: A Humble Opinion on Salt Administration Reform (Continued) 64

— Li Youyi

(B) Allow people to freely buy and sell without regional restrictions. If merchants are unwilling to transport to remote areas, there is a risk of salt shortage. (C) Currently, salt tax revenue ranks second in central government income, which is crucial to finance. Once the monopoly merchants are abolished, the entire tax revenue will be reduced to scattered amounts, which is feared to be unreliable. (D) Monopoly merchants are rich in capital. When the country is in urgent need, they can pre-collect future tax payments at any time or provide loans. Private merchants with limited capital cannot do this. For the above reasons, although the Central Salt Administration Reform Committee has been established for several years, it has not made any active and concrete progress. Only in a passive aspect, in the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932), the central and regional salt affairs administrative organs were all merged into the Salt Revenue Audit Bureau and the provincial branches, slightly reducing administrative expenses. However, the monopoly rights of salt merchants remain the same. The lives of salt farmers are difficult, and farmers and poor laborers still eat high-priced salt. Abandoning the fundamentals and focusing on the trivial is not a fundamental solution. Moreover, after the Salt Revenue Audit Bureau took over the salt affairs administration and management of anti-smuggling, the unified authority should be able to invigorate and benefit the country. However, a closer look at its achievements inevitably leads to disappointment. Those who govern salt affairs should adhere to the principle of preventing smuggling, facilitating sales, and increasing tax revenue. If the number of salt sales is ignored and the tax rate is simply increased to increase revenue, it is a bad policy. My country's salt tax in the late Qing Dynasty was only tens of millions of yuan per year. By the time of the Republic of China, the central government actively reorganized it, and the annual revenue gradually increased. Around the tenth year of the Republic (1921), it was about one hundred million yuan. After the sixteenth and seventeenth years of the Republic (1927-1928), it increased to one hundred million several tens of thousands of yuan. In recent years, there have been even more increases, leaping forward. It cannot be said that the tax revenue is not huge. However, if we look at the amount of salt released over the years, compared with the past ten years, it has mostly been between 3.67 million to 3.8 million "dan", with a difference of no more than one or two hundred thousand "dan". The number of salt released does not increase sharply with the prosperity of tax revenue, so it is clear that the increase in tax revenue is not due to salt sales. Since the Republic of China, additional taxes have been common, such as the central government's additional military purchase, post-war military expenses, and local additional provincial treasury surcharges, continuous provincial treasury surcharges, provincial public debt surcharges, and education expenses (there may be more that cannot be listed in detail). In the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), the additional taxes of each province were uniformly collected by the central government. After the Salt Revenue Audit Bureau took over the salt affairs administration, the Sima scale for measuring salt catties was changed to the market scale (the market scale is about 70-80% of the Sima scale, that is, each "dan" of salt was 100 catties in the past, but now it is only 70-80 catties). Reducing the weight without reducing the tax means that the tax rate has invisibly increased by 20-30%. No wonder the tax revenue has been more prosperous in recent years. However, this is like drinking poison to quench thirst, only caring about the present. Such a policy will lead to more smuggling, and the harms are countless. Aren't the two salt yards in Liangzhe, Yu and Dai, facing the problem of manufacturers stopping the purchase of salt catties due to the sluggish sales of official salt? If official sales are sluggish, private sales will be prosperous. This is an undeniable truth. It is also heard that smugglers are very active in the Pudong area of Shanghai, which further proves the increase in smuggling. I fear that in a few years, the more the tax increases, the more sluggish the sales will be. The tax revenue may temporarily increase, but the amount of salt released will decrease day by day. Driving all the poor people in the country to eat smuggled salt will also make the tax source unsustainable. This is a deep concern, and the government cannot but take it into account. However, it is difficult to change the accumulated malpractices of hundreds of years overnight. Only by gradually rectifying and improving can we achieve perfection. I used to work in salt administration in the Song District for six years. When Zou Yulin was the head of the Salt Office, he ordered each district to compile the first chapter of the salt administration history, and I was the main writer for the Song District. I personally experienced the salt-producing areas and witnessed the plight of salt farmers. I often lamented that salt farmers and salt merchants are both people in the salt industry. Why are their hardships and joys so different? Now that the government is striving for reform, aiming to benefit the country and the people, based on the experience I have gained over the years, within the scope of my limited knowledge, I have slightly considered the new salt law and prepared the following preliminary reform opinions: (1) Increase the purchase price of salt to help salt farmers and prevent private sales. Most of the edible salt produced in our country is in the coastal areas of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Fujian, Shandong, Hebei, and the three northeastern provinces. The people are poor and fierce, and the land is eroded by the tide and cannot be cultivated. They rely entirely on extracting brine to make salt to make a living. However, the prices at which salt merchants purchase salt catties from salt farmers in various places are very low. Even in Liangzhe, where the cost is relatively high, each "dan" is only one or two yuan. In other areas, it is as low as two or three jiao. Compared with the selling price of salt by merchants, the difference is very large. Some harsh manufacturers even suppress the weight when weighing it into the factory warehouse. Salt farmers cannot bear the hardship. Smugglers take the opportunity to purchase at a higher price, steal and make profits. Salt farmers are forced by livelihood. Knowing that it is illegal, they are happy to sell smuggled salt, which makes smuggled salt flood the country. Try to calculate carefully, and the annual private sales should be an alarming number (this calculation will be detailed later). Furthermore, the salt farmers themselves are all countless ignorant people. If the purchase price is too low, they have no choice but to sell smuggled salt in the hope of getting a good price. This is what the timid do. The fierce ones even follow the smugglers and transport salt with weapons, eventually becoming bandits and disrupting the local area. This is unavoidable. Modern pirates in our country, such as Mao, are related to this. The harm is not only in the salt administration. We must seek remedies urgently and cannot delay. The government should quickly investigate the living conditions of salt farmers in various regions and increase the purchase price of salt, so that the coastal people can have sufficient food and clothing and not be tempted by smugglers. We will see that the harm of smuggled salt will be eliminated without enforcement. Then teach them to improve salt production so that the salt is clean and hygienic. This is the most important fundamental measure (the salt produced in our country, except for well and pool salt, is slightly better in the Zhejiang, Fujian, and Song districts. The salt in Huai and Lu contains a lot of mud and impurities, which hinders hygiene when eaten). (To be continued)

Decline of Chinese Cotton Mills: Dasheng No. 2 Mill Ceases Operations 69

Accountant Xie Lin Appointed as Liquidator; No. 1 and No. 3 Mills Continue Normal Operations

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that Chinese cotton mills are suffering from the impact of the global economic downturn and the decline of the rural economy, resulting in a lack of purchasing power. Business is extremely depressed, and work stoppages and layoffs occur from time to time. Dasheng No. 2 Cotton Mill has also entered the vortex, unable to maintain operations, and has announced its closure. Accountant Xie Lin has been appointed as liquidator. History of Dasheng

Dasheng No. 1 Textile Company: 75,380 spindles, 2,000 thread spindles, 725 looms, located in Nantong, managed by Li Shengbo. Dasheng No. 1 Textile Company Auxiliary Factory: 16,724 spindles, 240 looms, located in Nantong, managed by Li Shengbo. Dasheng No. 2 Textile Company: 35,000 spindles, 240 looms, located in Jiulong Town, Qidong, managed by Shen Yanmou. Dasheng No. 3 Textile Company: 30,340 spindles, 1,200 thread spindles, 594 looms, located in Changle Town, Haimen, managed by Shen Yanmou. The above companies have a head office at 392 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, but the capital is independent.

Closure and Liquidation

Dasheng No. 2 Textile Company has a capital of 1.4 million taels. Recently, due to the impact of the economic downturn, it has encountered financial difficulties. The Qidong factories have long been closed. It has now been decided to cease operations and liquidate, and accountant Xie Lin has been appointed as liquidator. The following is Xie Lin's announcement: Notice: The undersigned accountant has been appointed as liquidator of Dasheng No. 2 Textile Co., Ltd. and assumed office on November 1st. In addition to reporting to the court in accordance with the law, this is a special announcement. Zhengze Accounting Firm, 723 Continental Commercial Building, Nanjing Road, Shanghai.

Shareholders' Meeting

Dasheng No. 1 Company, its auxiliary factory, and Dasheng No. 3 Company are all operating normally and have scheduled an extraordinary shareholders' meeting. The notice states that the number of vacancies on the board of directors of both companies has exceeded one-third of the total number of directors. In accordance with Article 143 of the Company Law, supplementary elections must be held. It has been decided by the meeting to hold the first extraordinary shareholders' meeting of the company at 2:00 PM on November 15th at the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association, 4th floor, Xizang Road, Shanghai. The extraordinary shareholders' meeting of the third company will be held at the same location at 2:00 PM on November 16th. The matter is of utmost importance. We hope that you will attend on time. If you are unable to attend in person due to unforeseen circumstances, please entrust a representative to attend the meeting, and please bring your stock certificate or seal to the Dasheng Shanghai Office, 4th floor, Baoanfang, Nanjing Road, Shanghai, five days before the meeting to receive the admission ticket, voting card, election ticket, etc. Stock transfers will be suspended from the date of this announcement until the date of the meeting. In addition to separate letters, this is a special announcement. Issued by the Board of Directors of Dasheng No. 1 and No. 3 Textile Companies.

Compulsory Registration of Smokers Begins Yesterday 71

Lenient Treatment for Those Who Register Voluntarily

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Smoker Registration Section began handling the registration of all smokers in Shanghai on July 1st and ended on October 31st, with a total of over 23,000 registered smokers. Yesterday was the start of the compulsory registration period. In order to be considerate of smokers, the bureau will exempt those who voluntarily go to register from punishment. At the same time, the police will arrest smokers and send them to the South City General Bureau or various branch bureaus for registration, also exempting them from punishment. However, from today onwards, in addition to lenient treatment for those who voluntarily go to the bureau to register and no punishment will be imposed, those who are arrested will be dealt with in accordance with the law, either with a fine or a prison sentence. According to news from the section yesterday, approximately 2,000 smokers were registered in the North and South Cities on yesterday alone.

According to the Dagong News Agency, as compulsory registration begins, the Municipal Public Security Bureau should strictly investigate and arrest unregistered smokers. Starting yesterday, in addition to ordering the police from various branch bureaus to pay attention to detaining and sending smokers to the General Bureau for interrogation, it has also specially dispatched investigators from the sections and a police platoon to conduct investigations separately. Personnel have also been dispatched to the remaining water and land transportation docks to conduct regular inspections. Many smokers have been arrested. Yesterday, more than 70 smokers were sent to the General Bureau by various branch bureaus. Since there was no record, the bureau ordered all the smokers sent to be interrogated and sent for drug detoxification immediately upon arrival. The work is very intense.

Nanjing Road Merchants' Association Continues to Oppose Telephone Rate Increase 72

Letter Sent to the Public Works Department Yesterday Reaffirming Previous Resolutions; Another Meeting Today to Discuss Countermeasures

Although the city's various public groups have strongly protested the telephone rate increase proposal, there has been no positive news. In order to redouble their efforts and express their opposition, the Nanjing Road Merchants' Association sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, requesting that the report of the four experts not be approved. It is also concentrating its efforts and will convene a meeting of all members today to discuss countermeasures. The China East News Agency reporter has investigated and filed the following report:

Yesterday's Meeting: According to Zhao Tingyu, the person in charge of the Nanjing Road Merchants' Association, the association has repeatedly argued against the telephone company's rate increase. During the review by the expert committee, it also sent two letters stating the reasons why the rate should not be increased, urging them to pay attention. The report submitted by the experts has been seen in the newspapers, and it still does not take into account the current economic and commercial situation and the public interest. Instead, it rashly proposed a rate increase plan, and its calculations are flawed. If the cost of each call is three cents, then stores should be entitled to at least 300 calls per month for the ten yuan they spend. Therefore, the matter was discussed at a meeting yesterday, and it was resolved to send a letter to the Public Works Department, requesting them to seriously consider it and not approve it, in order to benefit business and reassure the public.

Letter to the Public Works Department: The association's letter to the Public Works Department yesterday stated: "We are writing to you because our association has repeatedly argued against the Shanghai Telephone Company's telephone rate increase and has submitted the reasons why the rate should not be increased one by one, hoping that the expert committee would adopt them and make a fair resolution. However, we recently read the summary of the report submitted by the telephone experts to your bureau in the Chinese newspapers. All members of our association have studied it carefully and feel that it overemphasizes the excessive praise of the company, which is used as a basis for prioritizing the company's interests. Although it mentions the company's excessive consumption and salaries, it is nothing more than a smokescreen. It does not take into account the public users' ability to pay or their interests. Lowering the basic telephone fee slightly is pleasing to the ear, but the basic number of calls is reduced as much as possible, which is actually more costly. Even smart children will not be fooled, let alone users. The price of extra calls is too high, and large stores with a large scope of business will naturally have busy calls. Charging them all will be even more unfair. According to a gentleman who recently returned from London, the London Telephone Company reduced the quarterly fee from one pound twelve shillings and six pence to one pound six shillings due to the shared feeling of economic downturn. The fees in various places, which were previously one pound seven shillings and six pence, have been reduced to one pound. The prices for group business and business are also considerably lower, averaging 30% off. London has a high cost of living, but it still reduces telephone fees, while Shanghai has a low cost of living but increases telephone fees. This reason is difficult to understand. In short, Shanghai is now facing economic difficulties and a declining market. No matter what clever method the telephone company uses to increase rates, the city's users simply do not want to bear it. Please, bureau, consider the public interest carefully and do not approve it. In this way, the citizens' hard-earned money, which they use to fulfill their tax obligations, will still have some rights that they can rely on your bureau to protect, which will not be in vain."

Another Meeting Today: The association believes that the telephone company's move is truly inappropriate. Although the four experts know that there are reasons to increase rates, they absolutely do not ask whether citizens have the ability to pay the extra fees. Although it has sent letters to the Public Works Department and the Taxpayers' Association again, it has not seen any results so far. For the sake of caution, it will convene a meeting of all members again at 4:00 PM today to discuss further countermeasures in order to achieve the goal as soon as possible. It is also known that members of the association have already put forward new opinions, which will be discussed in detail at today's meeting.

Page 11

He Bingxian Discusses Foreign Trade in the First Half of This Year 75

Trade Values, Both Exports and Imports, Showed a Decline; Imports of Staple Foods Increased

He Bingxian, Director of the Bureau of International Trade, in order to explain the decline in China's total trade value for the first half of this year, the nature of the decline, the trade balance, the state of gold and silver movements, the rise and fall of major import and export commodities, and the changes in trade by country and port, yesterday released the following statement analyzing China's foreign trade:

Trade Values: Observing trade values, since 1932, China's foreign trade has experienced a sharp decline. The total value of foreign trade in 1932 decreased by 4% compared to 1931, 1933 decreased by 9% compared to 1932, and 1934 decreased by 3% compared to 1933. Up to the first half of this year, although China's foreign trade has not reversed the previous decline with an increase, the degree of the decline this year has slightly eased. The total value of China's foreign trade in the first half of this year was 804,824,968 yuan, a decrease of only 4% compared to the same period in 1934. Analyzing import and export trade, the export trade volume in the first half of this year was 259,369,673 yuan, a decrease of 3.42% compared to the same period last year, and the import trade volume was 545,455,295 yuan, a decrease of 4.6% compared to the same period last year. The decline in the value of China's import trade in the first half of this year was partly due to the decline in import prices and partly due to the decrease in import volume.

Trade Balance: In the first half of this year, China's import surplus totaled 286,085,622 yuan, a decrease of more than 15,219,000 yuan compared to the same period last year. During China's extreme currency contraction, the decrease in the import surplus is not unwelcome. However, we should note that the decrease in the import surplus is not due to an increase in export volume, but only because the rate of decline in import volume is higher than the rate of decline in export volume. In the first ten days of this year, the percentage of the import surplus in the total import value was still 52.45, which is no different from 52.87 in the same period last year. The movement of gold and silver is closely related to the trade balance. In the first half of this year, due to the government's restrictions on the export of silver and encouragement of silver imports, silver turned from a net export to a net import. In terms of gold and gold coins, there was also a net export this year. Generally, the net export of gold and silver accounted for about 7% of China's commodity import surplus in the first half of this year. From this, it can be seen that in the first half of this year, China's hard currency only offset a very small part of the commodity import surplus, and most of the commodity import surplus still needs to rely on invisible income or be offset in the next period.

Trade Nature: Observing from the nature of commodity trade, the distribution of China's import and export commodities in the first half of this year has changed significantly compared to last year. On the export side, due to the sharp decline in textile products, the percentage of manufactured goods has decreased. As a result, raw materials and semi-finished products have jumped to first place, manufactured goods have retreated to second place, and food, beverages, and tobacco remain in third place. On the import side, there have also been changes. Manufactured goods rank first, the import of rice and grains has increased sharply, so food, beverages, and tobacco have advanced to second, and raw materials and semi-finished products have retreated to third. If the value of various commodities in the first half of this year is compared with the same period last year, on the export side, raw materials and semi-finished products increased by 15% compared to the first half of last year, food, beverages, and tobacco also increased by 4%, while manufactured goods decreased by 23%. In addition, miscellaneous goods also decreased by more than 8%. On the import side, valued in gold units, food, beverages, and tobacco increased by 34%, manufactured goods increased by more than 7%, and miscellaneous goods increased by 25%, while raw materials and semi-finished products decreased by more than 8%.

Import Commodities: In the first half of this year, the total value of China's imported foreign goods, valued in national currency, was 545,455,000 yuan, a decrease of 4.28% compared to 569,849,000 yuan in the same period last year. Among the various imported commodities, rice and grains had the largest value, followed by metals, and then cotton, timber, kerosene, dyes, pigments, chemical products, and pharmaceuticals. Sugar and paper each were valued at more than 10 million gold units. In addition, cotton cloth, vehicles, gasoline, wool fabrics, diesel, fish, seafood were each valued at between 5 million and 10 million gold units.

Export Commodities: Last year, China's exported commodities were mostly hides and furs. This year, tung oil jumped to first place, followed by metal ores, and then hides and furs. In addition, preserved eggs and egg products, tea, and peanuts were each valued at more than 10 million yuan. Raw silk, cotton yarn, wool, drawnwork and embroidery, silk fabrics, and pig bristles were each between 5 million and 10 million yuan. Other important export commodities included sausage casings, cotton, medicinal herbs, spices, livestock, fruits, vegetables, tobacco, and coal, all around several million yuan. Those with decreases rather than increases included tea, medicinal materials, spices, fruits, vegetables, straw hats and straw hat braids, pig bristles, mats, and eggs and egg products. Generally, among China's exported commodities in the first half of this year, those with decreases were more numerous than those with increases.

Trade by Country: Regarding the increase or decrease in China's trade with various countries in the first half of this year, exports increased significantly to Italy, Germany, Australia, the United States, Korea, and France. Exports decreased to the Dutch East Indies, Japan, India, the Soviet Union, Hong Kong, the United Kingdom, Siam, and Annam. On the import side, imports increased the most from Australia, followed by Siam. In addition, imports from Annam, Japan, and Germany also increased. Imports from the United States, Hong Kong, the United Kingdom, the Dutch East Indies, India, the Soviet Union, France, and Korea decreased.

Trade by Port: The rise and fall of foreign trade in various Chinese ports in the first half of this year is also worth noting. Comparing the first half of this year with the same period last year, on the export side, Qingdao, Shantou, Hankou, Nanjing, Wuhu, Yantai, Gongbei, and Mengzi all increased. Shanghai, Tianjin, Guangzhou, Kowloon, Xiamen, Ningbo, Fuzhou, Jiangmen, Wuzhou, and Qinhuangdao decreased. On the import side, compared with the same period last year, Tianjin, Qingdao, Shantou, Chaobei, Wuzhou, Hankou, and Ningbo increased, while Shanghai, Guangzhou, Kowloon, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Jiangmen, Mengzi, Nanjing, Jiujiang, Wuhu, Yantai, and Qinhuangdao decreased.

Trend Summary: In summary, we can summarize the trends in China's foreign trade for the first half of this year into the following points: (1) In terms of trade values, both exports and imports decreased in the first half of this year compared to the same period last year, but the degree of decline seems to have eased compared to before. According to our research, the decline in exports this year is still due to the decrease in export volume, and the reason for the decrease in export volume is closely related to the high silver prices and prolonged exchange rates in recent years. The decline in import values is the result of a decrease in both import prices and import volume. (2) In the first half of this year, because the degree of decline in exports was not as severe as the decline in imports, the import surplus decreased compared to the same period last year, and the gold and silver export surplus decreased due to the government's restrictions on silver exports and encouragement of silver imports. From this, it can be seen that China's trend of using precious metals to offset commodity import surpluses has greatly decreased in the first half of this year. (3) In commodity trade, on the import side, three major staple grains - rice, wheat, and flour - all increased in the first half of this year compared to the same period last year. This is naturally due to the disasters last year. Building materials and production tools, such as machinery, timber, and metals, also increased compared to last year. This is due to the development of China's economic construction in recent years. However, cotton has decreased significantly. In addition, other consumer goods have either increased or decreased, generally not differing much from last year. On the export side, tung oil, metals, ores, peanuts, drawnwork and embroidery, coal, and sausage casings increased compared to last year, livestock and tobacco maintained their original state, and others such as cotton yarn, silk, tea, egg products, hides and furs, wool, silk fabrics, cotton, cotton cloth, and pig bristles all decreased. Although there have also been some changes in trade by country and port, they are generally the same as in previous years.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests an Increase in Import Taxes on Foreign Silk Fabrics 78

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to increase import taxes on foreign silk fabrics. The submission reads: Regarding the request, on the 31st of this month, the Electrical Machinery Factory Trade Association and the Silk Fabric Trade Association jointly sent a letter stating that the previous letter from our associations requesting your chamber to forward to the government a request to refund the import tax on artificial silk raw materials in order to help the foreign trade had been approved by the Ministry of Finance with Guan Zi No. 7271, which stated: "We have received your submission and learned that refunding the import tax on artificial silk raw materials is related to helping the domestic silk industry, and the request cannot be approved. Please be informed." We can see that the government's assistance to the domestic silk industry is comprehensive and meticulous. However, the current situation of the domestic silk weaving industry is that silk prices have plummeted, business is declining, foreign trade sales are almost non-existent, domestic market sales are also decreasing, and the trend of decline is increasing day by day. The reasons are many, but the surge in imports of foreign artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics is a major blow. The reason for the surge in imports is that the import tax rate on artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics is not only not balanced with the import tax on artificial silk raw materials, but is also lower. Therefore, it is easier to dump products in China to achieve low costs and high profits. The collection of import tax on artificial silk raw materials has always been based on quantity, not price, while the collection of import tax on artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics is based on price, not quantity. In 1920, the import tax rate on artificial silk was 58 gold units per Chinese dan, equivalent to about 120 yuan in national currency. At that time, the value of artificial silk was about 100 yuan in national currency per Chinese dan, so the import tax rate per dan of artificial silk was 60% of the value. The import tax on artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics was 80% of the value, so it was still balanced. Foreign artificial silk fabrics could not be dumped in China. Now, the import tax on artificial silk has been changed to 1.20 gold units per kilogram, equivalent to about 2.4 yuan in national currency, while the current value of artificial silk is only about 0.9 yuan per kilogram, so the import tax rate per kilogram is as high as 250% of the value. However, the import tax rate on artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics has not been changed, so the difference between the raw material tax and the product tax is huge. Foreign merchants are taking advantage of this by turning to manufacturing fabrics and importing them in large quantities, sucking the lifeblood of our domestic silk weaving industry. If dumping is allowed to continue without restraint, the impact will not only disrupt market prices, but also have unimaginable consequences for the national economy and people's livelihood. Our associations feel the pain deeply and cannot remain silent. We are writing to your chamber to request that you forward this to the government and promptly correct the tax rate, clearly ordering the customs to increase the import tax rate on artificial silk fabrics and blended fabrics, or to reduce the import tax on artificial silk raw materials, so that the import tax rates on raw materials and fabrics are balanced, in order to prevent large-scale imports of foreign silk, maintain the precarious survival of domestic silk, strive to compete with foreign silk, and restore silk sales in order to provide relief. We have learned that the current import tariff rules of the customs impose an import tax on foreign silk fabrics, whether the raw material is cocoon silk or artificial silk, at a rate of 80% of the value. However, because the import of artificial silk is currently taxed on a per-quantity basis, it reaches 250% of the value according to the market price. Therefore, foreign merchants are changing their plans and importing them in large quantities by converting them into fabrics, which is more profitable. Our country's weaving factories, in turn, have difficulty competing due to the heavy tax on raw materials. The purpose of heavy taxation on manufactured goods to protect domestic factories is counterproductive. The request of the two associations to amend the above import tax rate and strive to balance the raw material tax rate and the fabric tax rate is an essential plan to protect weaving factories. We hereby submit this request to your ministry for review and approval for implementation, which would be fair and convenient.

The Miscellaneous Grains Association Encourages Oil Mills to Resume Operations First 79

—Oil Mills Indicate They Will Only Resume Operations After the Bran Surcharge Is Cancelled—

Since the oil cake factories and transporters in various regions went on strike and ceased operations in protest against the imposition of an additional tax on bran in Guangdong Province, it has been two months, and they are still continuing to persist. The Municipal Miscellaneous Grains Association, in consideration of agricultural production and the livelihoods of workers, has specially encouraged the oil mills to resume operations first. However, due to the burden, the oil mills have indicated that they will only resume operations after the bran surcharge is cancelled. Otherwise, they are determined to sacrifice business. The details of the situation have been reported by a Dagongshe reporter as follows:

The Miscellaneous Grains Association Encourages Resumption of Operations

The Municipal Miscellaneous Grains Association yesterday sent a letter to the Oil Mill Association encouraging resumption of operations. The original letter stated: "Dear Sirs, Since the imposition of an additional tax on bran in Guangdong Province, factories and transporters in various regions have ceased operations for more than two months. The All-China Federation of Miscellaneous Grains and Oil Cake Industries is currently striving to have this surcharge cancelled. However, it is now the time for new soybeans to be harvested. If the oil mills continue to suspend operations, the soybeans will be unsalable, and farmers in the producing areas will be in dire straits. Transporters engaged in soybeans will also have their livelihoods cut off. Considering the various oil mills, the workers' lives are also difficult to maintain. This has a negative impact on agriculture, industry, and commerce. After weighing the gains and losses and making overall plans, our association believes that the bran surcharge should be vigorously opposed, but the oil mills' suspension of operations can be handled flexibly. For the sake of the livelihood of farmers, transporters, and oil mill workers in the soybean producing areas, it seems possible to resume operations first. Therefore, we are sending this letter to you. Whether it is appropriate, we hope your association will consider and handle it accordingly."

Oil Mills Indicate They Will Strive to Eliminate the Bran Surcharge

The Oil Mill Trade Association replied to the letter from the Miscellaneous Grains Association, stating: "Dear Sirs, We have received your letter stating that it is now the time for new soybeans to be harvested, and for the sake of the livelihood of farmers, transporters, and oil mill workers in the soybean producing areas, it seems possible to resume operations first. We acknowledge this. The sales of bean cakes and peanut cakes produced by the oil mills in our city have always been mainly in Guangdong Province. Since Guangdong Province imposed an additional surcharge, domestic cakes are treated the same as Northeast cakes, with the same tax rate. It is difficult to compete with them. The Guangdong Province cake sales market will be monopolized by Northeast cakes, with no room for domestic cakes. If we resume operations before the surcharge is cancelled, the bean cakes produced will have no sales and will inevitably be stored for a long time and become moldy, increasing losses. Rather than suffering even greater losses after resuming operations, we would rather suspend operations to strive for the cancellation of the surcharge. We hereby reply to you, and we hope you will take this into consideration." Signed, Shanghai Oil Mill Trade Association.

Telegraphic Urging of Representatives from Various Regions to Come to Shanghai

The All-China Federation of Oil Cake and Miscellaneous Grains Industries telegraphed the Miscellaneous Grains Trade Associations in Jinan, Kaifeng, Xuzhou, Bengbu, Qingdao, and Hankou, requesting them to send representatives to Shanghai as soon as possible to participate in the petition. The original telegram stated: "In order to strive for the cancellation of the additional agricultural special tax on bran in Guangdong Province, the All-China Federation of Oil Cake and Miscellaneous Grains Industries requests that representatives be sent to Shanghai to participate in the joint meeting held on the 29th of last month. It was decided to organize the 'Federation for Requesting the Cancellation of the Additional Agricultural Special Tax on Bran in the All-China Oil Cake and Miscellaneous Grains Industries,' and a committee was appointed to start working immediately. It was also decided to jointly go to Beijing on the 8th of this month to petition the Fifth National Congress. We hope that you will promptly appoint representatives and come to Shanghai before the 8th of this month to jointly plan the next steps. Please let us know in advance."

The Literacy Education Committee Holds a Guidance and Inspection Meeting 80

The second session of the municipal literacy schools run by the Municipal Literacy Education Committee is about to begin for the second month. The students are still enthusiastic. Recently, in order to prevent student absenteeism, the committee convened a discussion meeting at the Municipal Government on October 28, inviting the heads of all municipal public security sub-bureaus and the directors of various district offices. The following measures were decided: (1) Each public security sub-bureau will assign a special commissioner to be responsible for handling literacy education matters, and will select several capable police officers to carry out the work together. (2) When summoning students, teachers will accompany the police officers to identify them. The time will be determined by the teachers in consultation. (3) Whether a student is at home will be based on whether the household registration has been reported as moved, to prevent false reports. (4) In order to facilitate communication between the public security bureau and the district schools, each public security sub-bureau will prepare a sign-in book and hand it over to the teachers of each literacy school for safekeeping. The commissioner sent by each public security bureau will visit each literacy school once a week for inspection and sign the sign-in book during the inspection for evaluation. (5) Each public security sub-bureau and the director of each district must hold a discussion meeting at least once a month. (6) For the sake of further accuracy in the investigation of illiterate people, each director will consult with the investigation committee, or cooperate with the public security bureau when investigating households. In addition, an inspection meeting was held at the Municipal Government on October 30. It is reported that the directors and inspectors of the Municipal Government and the committee attended. The items that should be noted during the inspection, such as teaching and management, were discussed in detail and listed for distribution.

Page 12

The Zhejiang General Association Telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government to Request the Abolition of the Household Tax for the Security Corps 81

The Zhejiang General Association telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government yesterday to request the abolition of the household tax for the Security Corps in order to reduce the burden on the people. The original text reads: "We have learned that the collection of the household tax for the Security Corps in Zhejiang Province was previously considered by the Ministry of Finance to be a property tax and should not be allocated on a per-household basis, resulting in apportionment. This household tax should be incorporated into the property tax. We respectfully request that your government correct this matter. However, your government still uses the amount of land owned by each household as the standard for differentiated taxation. This not only fails to understand the central government's concern for the people's difficulties and cultivation of the national foundation, but also the management of the Security Corps' expenses and the training and command are unified at the district level, and the districts are unified at the provincial level. The burden on the people who freely contribute to each county is endless, and the amount actually used for the teams is limited. Moreover, the fertility of the land in each county, the thinness of the products, the poverty and wealth of the people, the amount of tax revenue, and the severity of the bandits are all different. It is still difficult to raise funds, and it is not easy to control expenses. In order to reconcile surpluses and deficits, suit the economic path, and achieve the grand effect of practical and economical operation, we should earnestly abolish all illegal and trivial miscellaneous taxes collected locally and reduce the burden on the people. Therefore, Chairman Chiang issued the directive on the General Outline for Improving the Security System in Various Provinces. The provincial governments should earnestly follow this spirit and not deviate from Chairman Chiang's original intention of relieving the people's suffering. Moreover, in September of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the Finance Department and the Security Office submitted twelve measures, which were presented to Chairman Chiang and telegraphed, and the item of land tax in the measures was clearly ordered not to be increased. It is even more inappropriate to avoid the name but maintain the reality, still using the land as the standard for taxation, and borrowing the household tax as a disguised land tax, which violates Chairman Chiang's grand intention of improvement. Moreover, the Haicheng County Security Corps' expenses are still charged from the original donation numbers on the spot. In addition, 0.5 yuan is levied on each yuan of grain as a household tax to be sent to the province. This is an uncompensated additional burden on top of the original Security Corps donation, a disguised increase in taxes. This is not only unbearable for the people's strength, but also how can it show the country's great credibility? The county magistrates of each county, or feel that the training and command of the Security Corps are concentrated in the province and cannot achieve the practical effect of local defense, therefore, they separately establish new names and open up new taxes. For example, the Longquan County Gangkun Strongmen Brigade even wants to levy an additional eight yuan per mu, although your government considers the people's difficulties and is still cautiously reviewing it and has not yet approved it, but I am afraid that the various counties that imitate this will be endless. The melon of Huangtai, holding the vine is worrying. After deliberation at the members' congress of our association, in order to take care of political credibility and express the people's difficulties, we respectfully request that your government follow the central government and Chairman Chiang's intention to reduce the burden on the people, and incorporate the household tax for the Security Corps into the property tax. The families of the people are not rich, and originally did not become thieves. They are not required to practice group defense and have no need to be protected. Therefore, they should not be on the burden list, and should be exempted from collection. In addition to the household donations and shop donations of the Security Corps in various places in the past, all should be abolished in order to establish political credibility and relieve the people's difficulties. Sincerely. The Zhejiang General Association."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Explains the Stamp Duty Regulations for Lease Contracts and House Tickets 82

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Wufeng Company to explain the stamp duty regulations for lease contracts and house tickets: "We have received your letter of the 31st of this month and fully understood the contents. Article 16, Section 10 of the Stamp Tax Law stipulates that lease documents and contracts must be affixed with a stamp worth 2 cents per document, and those who use booklets to collect rent must affix a stamp worth 2 jiao per year, and those with a lease amount of less than 10 yuan per document are exempt from stamping. Therefore, according to the above regulations, (1) each lease contract must be affixed with a stamp worth 2 cents, and those less than 10 yuan are exempt from stamping; (2) if house tickets are used instead of booklets to collect rent, they are also considered lease documents, and each one must be affixed with a stamp worth 2 cents, and those less than 10 yuan are exempt from stamping; (3) when renting a house, the middleman and guarantor are jointly signing the lease contract, and there is no so-called independent guarantee. What kind of guarantee are you referring to in your letter? Please reply."

The Ministry of Communications Approves the Merchant Ship Captains' Association: Maritime Arbitration Body to be Established Soon 83

The Ordinance on Handling Maritime Disputes Has Been Submitted to the Legislative Yuan for Deliberation

The Shanghai Chinese Merchant Ship Captains' Association previously submitted a petition to the Ministry of Communications, which was then forwarded to the Judicial Yuan. The Judicial Yuan issued orders to all levels of courts, stating that before the establishment of maritime courts, the handling of shipping cases should involve inviting maritime experts to participate in the research and consultation, etc. Now, Approval No. 2699 from the Ministry of Communications has been received, stating, "The petition has been noted. The establishment of a maritime court was previously resolved by the Executive Yuan at its 162nd meeting. A maritime arbitration body should be established. The Ministry will, in conjunction with the Ministry of Judicial Administration and the Ministry of the Navy, formulate the regulations for the Maritime Dispute Resolution Committee, submit them to the Executive Yuan for approval, and then forward them to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. It is expected to be passed and promulgated soon. The request is deemed unnecessary. Please take note." This is the approval.

Rentsu Report: Economic Study Group Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 84

Visiting Mayor Wu Today, Touring Hangzhou on the 5th

The economic study group of fourteen members, organized by the Japanese Rentsu News Agency, arrived in Shanghai yesterday at 6:30 PM from Nanjing via Suzhou. After disembarking at the North Railway Station, they proceeded to the Fengyang Hotel for rest. They plan to stay in Shanghai for seven days to inspect the city's situation and plan to visit Hangzhou on the 5th to tour scenic spots. They are scheduled to return to Japan on the Shanghai Maru on the 7th. Details are as follows:

Arrival in Shanghai via Suzhou

The study group was organized by the Japanese Rentsu News Agency to commemorate the 35th anniversary of its founding, uniting people from Tokyo, Osaka, Nagoya, and other places. At the beginning of last month, they came to China from Japan and first visited Qingdao, Jinan, Tianjin, Beiping, Taiyuan, Datong, Zhangjiakou, Shijiazhuang, Hankou, and Nanjing. Along the way, they paid visits to local authorities. After arriving in Nanjing on the 29th, they also paid visits to the central authorities. According to the planned itinerary, on the evening of the 31st, they took the night express train from Nanjing to Suzhou, arriving at Suzhou Station at 5:05 AM yesterday. After disembarking, they went to the Panmen Japanese Hotel for rest and were entertained by the Japanese Consul in Suzhou. Afterward, they toured the famous scenic spots of Suzhou. At 4:27 PM, they took a train from Suzhou to Shanghai, arriving at 6:35 PM. Commissioner Wang Changchun of the Shanghai Municipal Government and representatives from the Japanese Consulate-General welcomed them at the station. After disembarking, they went to the Fengyang Hotel, which had been arranged in advance, for rest.

Continuous Banquets

The group is scheduled to visit Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Ambassador Arichi, Consul-General Ishiya, and the Commander of the Araki Naval Landing Force this morning, and also inspect the construction in the city center. They will attend a banquet hosted by Mayor Wu at the Xinghualou Restaurant in the evening. At noon on the 3rd, Mayor Wu will hold a reception at his private residence on Haig Road. On the morning of the 4th, they will have free time. At noon, they will attend a banquet hosted by Hata Hiroshi, president of the Japanese Shanghai Nippo newspaper. At 3 PM, Consul Iwai will hold a lecture. In the evening, Consul-General Ishiya will host a banquet at his official residence on Seymour Road. On the morning of the 5th, accompanied by Commissioner Wang Changchun of the Municipal Government, they will take the early express train to Hangzhou to tour the scenic spots of the Six Bridges and Three Temples, and attend a banquet hosted by the Japanese Consul in Hangzhou. The next morning, they will leave Hangzhou and return to Shanghai. In the evening, they will attend a banquet hosted by the Japanese Rentsu News Agency at the 63 Flower Garden. At 9 AM on the morning of the 7th, they will depart for Japan on the Japanese ship Shanghai Maru.

List of Members

The group consists of fourteen members in total, including five from Tokyo: Kiichi Hirota, Ryoichi Ueda, Masaki Suzui, Shoichi Suzuki, and Kaiun Mishima; four from Osaka: Riichi Ezaki, Kenji Mezaki, Tatsuro Fukui, and Tsunehiko Manaka; two from Nagoya: Chotaro Arakawa and Tadayoshi Kuroda; and also Goro Mikoshima, director of the Rentsu News Agency, Minoru Okudaira from the business department, and Eikai Sumita from the photography department. (Central News Agency)

Issuing a Statement

Yesterday, the Shanghai branch of the Rentsu News Agency issued a statement in Japanese on behalf of the study group. The translated version is as follows: "The Economic Inspection Group of the Republic of China, consisting of fourteen members initiated by the Japan Telegraph and Telephone News Agency to commemorate the 35th anniversary of its founding, departed from Tokyo on October 7th, passed through Kobe via the sea route, and landed in Qingdao on the 11th of this month. Then, via Jinan, they went to Beiping and Tianjin, and also visited Zhangjiakou, Datong, Taiyuan, and Shijiazhuang. Afterward, they went south to inspect Hankou and Wuchang, and via Nanjing and Suzhou, arrived in Shanghai today. During this one-month inspection, we have been warmly welcomed by officials and civilians of both China and Japan in various places, and have been provided with great convenience in our inspection, for which the group is deeply grateful. Historically, China and Japan, in order to maintain peace in the East and promote East Asian culture, have stood on the basis of mutual cooperation. Not only are they of the same script and race, but also their relationships have been particularly close since ancient times. In order to fulfill this mission, it seems necessary to intensify the relationship of mutual assistance in the economic sphere, to seek economic integration, and to strive for the independent development of the East Asian economy. The members of this inspection group are engaged in the manufacture of daily necessities in Japan and are also directly selling them in the market. They are particularly concerned about the movements of the Chinese economic sector on a daily basis. Today, we have arrived in Shanghai, the center of Chinese economic activity and the central port of Sino-Japanese trade, and we are very fortunate to have the opportunity to actually inspect it. We sincerely hope to bring back the lessons learned to our homeland and contribute to the mission of making the economies of China and Japan closer. On the occasion of our economic inspection group's arrival in Shanghai, we dare to express our humble opinions and hope for the support of officials and civilians on both sides of China and Japan." The Reduced Levy of Deed Tax in Shanghai County Extended Again 91

The Shanghai County Government has received an order from the provincial government to reduce the deed tax rate on the sale of houses by 6.3%, and the extension has been made several times until the end of October this year. It should have been levied at the tax rate of 9.6% for the sale, and no further extension will be granted. However, this year, the counties in northern Jiangsu suffered from yellow water disasters, and the autumn harvest in other counties was not very abundant. If the reduced levy is not continued, it will inevitably be beyond their ability and they will be reluctant to move forward, which is contrary to the way of enriching taxes and caring for the people. Now, from November of this year to the end of January of next year, the extension will be granted for another three months, and it will still be levied at 6.3% for the sale, and the surcharge shall not exceed half of the principal tax, in order to lighten the burden, etc. After receiving the order, the county government announced it to the public yesterday, urging them to pay taxes on all untaxed deeds during this extended period of reduced levy, so as not to make mistakes again.

The New Life Movement Plan in the Confucius Temple Area has Started Guidance and Implementation 96

The Public Security Bureau Dispatches Personnel to Lead the Guidance Team to Advise Shops and Residents to Comply

The Municipal Public Security Bureau has formulated a New Life Movement experimental zone plan. The plan and the measures for citizens in the Confucius Temple area to practice a new life were announced the day before yesterday. The details have been reported in previous news. It is now understood that the New Life Movement plan in the Confucius Temple area was implemented the day before yesterday (the 30th). The Inspection District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatched several personnel to the Confucius Temple area every day to lead the New Life Movement Labor Service Corps (i.e., the Guidance Team) to actively work by visiting shops and residents to advise them to implement it.
