Little Men (82) 152

— Original by Ms. Orcott of the United States, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

"Ah, I found it, I never get lost."

"There are three single roads here, how could you run so far?"

"Ah, the road is a bit far, but I often rest along the way."

"Isn't that thing very heavy?"

"That thing doesn't have a ring, I can't hold it very well, I often feel like my arms are going to break off."

"I wonder how the stationmaster would let you bring it," Tao Mo said again.

"I didn't say anything to him, he was in the ticket-selling room, he didn't see me, so I took it from the platform."

"Flang, run and tell them right away that the box has been picked up, so Mr. Tao won't worry," Mr. Pei said, seeing Nan En's expression of having done nothing wrong, and like others, he couldn't help but laugh.

Mrs. Pei was wiping the dust off Nan En's little face and admonishing her:

"I told you earlier that if the luggage didn't come, we would send someone to pick it up. In the future, you must wait patiently, if you run away yourself, it will cause trouble. You must promise me this, otherwise, I won't dare let you go out."

"Ah, then I won't run away anymore, but my father taught me not to delay things, so I didn't wait."

Education Lecture

The Cultivation of Elementary School Teachers (II) 153

— Wu Yan Yin

(Speech given to secondary school students nationwide on October 25th)

(II) Speaking from the perspective of elementary school teachers themselves, the responsibilities they bear are extremely significant. Our Master Mencius said, "To live in ease without education is akin to being an animal." The American educator Thorndike also said, "If young children never come into contact with adults and are not influenced by adult educational activities, then after twenty years, the majority of these children will die from smallpox, jaundice, malaria, and various epidemics. The remaining people will be unable to speak, ignorant of etiquette, and unable to use tools. Their lives will be little different from monkeys." It is evident that education is necessary, and education is a necessary method for continuing human civilization. Moreover, due to the pursuit of survival and comfort by humanity, everything is progressing "ceaselessly." Education is also a necessary method for teaching humanity to pursue benefits (the benefits of the masses) and avoid harm, and to advance civilization day by day. It not only continues the existing civilization but also "reforms the old and establishes the new," improving and promoting the existing civilization, and growing continuously. This is speaking from the perspective of general human civilization. Furthermore, considering the specific environment of a particular country, education is also essential for a country or nation to develop or survive in the world. The prosperity of imperialist countries is not solely reliant on the financial capital of a few capitalists; it is necessary to educate the majority of their people to believe that they are a "superior race," surpassing all so-called barbaric or semi-civilized peoples. It is necessary to educate the people to build a "Roman Empire," or a "Third Reich," or to fight desperately for the "Yamato spirit," for the so-called "lifeline of Japan," killing without batting an eye and plundering colonies and opening up resources without hesitation. Imperialist education has contributed to the prosperity of imperialism. Therefore, Germany's victory over France and Japan's victory over Germany are both attributed to elementary school teachers. Thus, in this economically depressed world, where most industries are almost at a standstill, elementary school education in Germany, Italy, and Japan has not been halted; on the contrary, it is valued even more than before. The impact on the treatment of elementary school teachers is also very small. Conversely, semi-colonial countries, such as our country and Abyssinia, have suffered from the lack of developed education. The physical strength of the people is weak, their knowledge is insufficient, and their will is not firm. Therefore, they cannot defeat imperialism in war. Hence, during the Sino-Japanese War, many traitors were used by the Japanese military. Therefore, when Italian troops entered Abyssinia, many Abyssinian tribes surrendered to the Italian army. In a period of severe national crisis, if we want to save ourselves from danger and revive the nation, the fundamental solution still relies on education and on elementary school teachers bearing the great responsibility. To continue and advance human civilization, or to save ourselves from danger and revive the nation, this cannot be accomplished by casual elementary school teachers who simply teach books all day long. Elementary school teachers must have heart, courage, perseverance, and methods to take on such a heavy responsibility. If elementary school teachers are to have heart, courage, perseverance, and methods, how can they not cultivate themselves? Even if we disregard the nation, speaking solely from the perspective of personal life, if elementary school teachers act casually and do not cultivate themselves, they will become sluggish, too far removed from the modern world, and will naturally fall behind and inevitably head towards the grave. We see many elementary school teachers who have worked as teachers for two or three decades and remain unknown, not only unable to "keep pace with the times" but also becoming "rigid" in everything, with everything out of step with the times. We also see many elementary school teachers who distinguish themselves, not only absorbing all that is new but also constantly making new contributions, spreading within the elementary school education community and influencing elementary school education in a locality or a nation. The division between these two types of elementary school teachers is due to one not pursuing further study while the other diligently studies and improves themselves. Of course, among the elementary school teachers who distinguish themselves, there are also those who are "purely stealing a reputation," but the majority have achieved success through the solid foundation gained from cultivation. Someone conducted a rough survey to investigate children's inclinations towards elementary school teachers. The results showed that the teachers most loved by children are those who are "knowledgeable and excellent," "skilled in teaching methods," "of noble character," and "enthusiastic in their work." Based on these inclinations, it can be seen that elementary school teachers must cultivate themselves if they want to be loved by their students.

Now, I want to talk about the methods of self-cultivation for elementary school teachers. The methods of self-cultivation for elementary school teachers can be divided into several points:

(I) Ideological Aspect: Elementary school teachers should have a firm and unwavering "belief," believing that human civilization will definitely move forward, believing that people should seek welfare for the majority, believing that imperialism and all evil forces that harm the majority will inevitably collapse one day, and that the "light" of the world will surely replace "darkness" and rise up. They must also have a thorough understanding of what kind of citizens are needed for present-day China and firmly believe that even if the country is destroyed, elementary school teachers can still cultivate useful citizens for the purpose of revival. How can such a belief be successfully cultivated? It is necessary to read more new books about world knowledge and social sciences on the one hand, and pay attention to the international situation, the cut-and-dried and dark aspects of society on the other hand, and study philosophy to understand the meaning of life and determine one's "outlook on life." In this way, education will have a center and will not be like "a blind man riding a blind horse, approaching a deep pool in the middle of the night," and everything can be handled with ease, and teaching materials and methods can be readily available.

(II) Character Aspect: Elementary school teachers should be clear about their own personalities. If they feel that they are too impatient, they must cultivate patience. If they feel that they are too slow, they must practice being quick and efficient in their work. When children oppose them, they should investigate the reasons and deal with them carefully, without losing their temper with the children. If they hear children say disrespectful things about them, they should not take it too seriously or put on airs of "the teacher is strict, and the Way is esteemed." When busy, they should not be negligent, and even less should they be easily impulsive and angry. When tired, they should not be afraid of trouble, anxious, or resentful of children. When sick, they should also restrain their temper. This is the method of cultivating patience. Prepare more in advance to avoid temporary haste, and practice diligently to improve your work efficiency. This is the method of practicing speed. The qualities needed by elementary school teachers, such as "sincerity," "compassion," "fair judgment," and "adaptability," are discussed in detail in various educational books. As for the methods of cultivating these qualities, they cannot be achieved solely by reading educational books. It is necessary to constantly experience things oneself, reflect on oneself, record one's shortcomings, or listen to others' criticisms, and strive to correct one's faults and do good. Reading biographies of educators is also an effective way to cultivate character.

(III) Physical Aspect: Elementary school teachers' work is extremely busy, and their responsibilities are extremely heavy. Naturally, they should maintain a healthy body. Everyone who is an elementary school teacher knows about health preservation methods, and there is no need for others to say more. However, everyone often neglects and slacks off and does not implement them. I believe that if the methods are too complicated, they will naturally be difficult to implement. If they are to be implemented, simple, easy-to-implement, and effective methods must be adopted and practiced regularly. I think that if you choose a sport that you enjoy and do it regularly, it will definitely be beneficial to your body. When all the children in the school are doing morning exercises, if the teachers join in, it will also have a great impact on their physical well-being. As for restrictive methods such as regulating diet and abstaining from smoking and alcohol, if you are determined to practice them, you will definitely be able to do so.

(IV) Knowledge Aspect: Elementary school teachers' knowledge should have two aspects: one is their basic knowledge, and the other is the knowledge applied in teaching. The method of increasing knowledge is to read more books on the one hand and to attend school or receive tutoring from famous teachers on the other hand. The method of reading books is to select several books, such as educational books and newspapers, books related to the subjects you teach, and books that you like to read. Set a schedule, create a form, and read step by step, annotating and summarizing as you go. If you can gather a group of people to organize a reading group, with each person reading separately and then reporting their findings at a certain time for everyone to study and discuss, then it will be more economical and effective than if each person reads individually. When attending summer school, summer training courses, or receiving tutoring from famous teachers, you should first examine your own shortcomings and needs, choose courses accordingly, and study hard. What books should elementary school teachers read? Many educational books have lists of recommended books, but we must carefully select a portion of these lists to read to avoid wasting effort and reading too many useless books.

(V) Skills Aspect: In addition to basic skills, elementary school teachers should also have teaching skills. The most important of the basic skills is the in-depth study of the skills related to the subjects they teach. If they can deeply study the skills related to the subjects they teach, they will have ample talent for teaching, not be flustered, and be able to demonstrate correctly and effectively. For example, writing, drawing, crafts, home economics, farming, industry, chemical and physical experiments, etc. If their own skills are not sufficient, how can they be competent and happy in the subjects they teach? Teaching skills include teaching methods, including "teaching attitude," "teaching voice," "ability to manage," "questioning method," "homework guidance method," "ability to cope," and "examination method," etc. Most of these are not easy to read about in books but must be personally experienced and tried. The methods to improve teaching skills are: (1) Self-reflection, which means always paying attention to one's own shortcomings and thinking about how to improve them. It is best to have a "self-reflection table," listing the skills that elementary school teachers should have one by one and including the percentage that each item should account for so that you can check yourself. These types of teacher self-reflection tables or teacher self-reflection standards can be found in various practical education books and do not need to be discussed further here. (2) Participating in research conferences to study issues related to teaching methods allows you to hear good opinions from others for your own reference and imitation. (3) Observing other people's teaching can also teach you many tricks. (4) Innovation and experimentation, which is the most important method for improving teaching skills. Try out good methods proposed by others and then research and modify them to create new methods, or if you feel that the methods you are implementing are not very effective, then think of a new method to try out and then research and modify it to create newer methods. In short, by working hard on your own and learning from others, your teaching skills will improve day by day.

The above are all about the personal self-cultivation methods of elementary school teachers. In addition, if education administrative authorities or elementary school principals want elementary school teachers' knowledge and skills to improve continuously, they should supervise elementary school teachers' further study, run summer schools, and force elementary school teachers to enroll. Issuing educational publications that study teaching methods, or designating certain educational books and forcing elementary school teachers to read them, is also a method. Organizing research conferences to guide elementary school teachers to attend research, is also a method. Furthermore, hiring experts, such as people who speak Mandarin fluently, musicians, and people with various skills, and using the method of circulating instruction to teach the teachers in each school to enhance the various skills of the teachers, is also a very effective method. Not every teacher can work hard on their own; many people still need to be urged by external forces. Therefore, education administrative authorities or elementary school principals must also pay close attention to the question of how to urge teachers to pursue further study.

Judging from the actual situation of elementary school education at present, elementary school teachers are extremely busy, working all day long without even time to rest, so where is there time for self-cultivation? Therefore, I also thought that if we really want elementary school teachers to cultivate themselves, the education administrative agencies should reduce the various work of elementary school teachers, especially the work of grading papers, which must be reduced to a minimum. Elementary school teachers themselves must also find ways to economize time, reducing papers and homework to a minimum, and assigning some of the work of grading papers to outstanding students to assist.

This speech of mine is all old news, but it may be helpful to normal school students who aspire to be good teachers. I hope you pay attention. As for how normal school students should cultivate themselves while they are normal school students, that is not within the scope of this issue, but I very much hope that you "learn to race horses before marrying," change your mentality of wanting to do great things in a vast world, do not despise practical work, and pay more attention to elementary school curriculum standards and other books and courses that elementary school teachers really need. Shen Bao Radio Weekly

Resistance-Coupled Push-Pull Radio 154

— Jian

—No Need to Use Inverting Vacuum Tubes—

(I) Reasons for Not Needing Inverting (Reversed Phase) Vacuum Tubes:

In an amplifier tube, the grid input voltage and the plate current are in the same phase (Same Phase). Therefore, it is in exactly the opposite phase to the plate output voltage. The so-called inverting vacuum tube is for this function.

Let us first observe the relationship between the voltage generated at the plate and the voltage generated at the filament: When the input voltage supplied to the grid is positive, the plate current increases and the plate voltage decreases, that is, the output voltage changes to negative. But the filament voltage increases instead, and the filament output voltage changes to positive. Therefore, the voltages generated at the plate and the filament are in exactly opposite phases.

Now, if the filament and plate ends are properly inserted into the grids of the push-pull tubes, the push-pull action can be easily completed without the need for an inverting tube.

(II) Connection Circuit: As shown in the first figure, the upper part is the ordinary resistance-coupled circuit. The difference is that, similar to the plate circuit, a load resistor is inserted in the filament circuit of the first vacuum tube, and its upper end is connected to the other tube of the push-pull circuit.

The vacuum tubes used are the No. 57 tube as the voltage amplifier tube, and the No. 45 or super No. 45 tube as the output tube. The reason for using triodes here is to make the sound reproduction accurate and to avoid odd harmonic distortion (especially third harmonic distortion).

Points to note on wiring:

(1) Connection of the negative grid resistor and the bypass capacitor of the No. 57 tube:

The capacitor inserted in parallel with the negative grid resistor cannot be grounded at one end as usual in this case, because if it is grounded, the load resistor will be short-circuited. Therefore, it must be inserted at both ends of the load resistor. If the bypass capacitor is not inserted, and no other load resistor is inserted, but the negative grid resistor itself is used as the load, it can work, although not perfectly.

(2) Load resistor inserted in the filament circuit:

The values of the signal voltages generated at the filament load and the plate load must be equal, and their phases must be opposite. Although the plate and filament are easily affected by the screen grid current, etc., it is usually sufficient to use loads with the same resistance value.

Experimental Ultra-Shortwave Oscillator 155

— Hua Meng

Here, I would like to introduce one or two simple and easy-to-experiment ultra-shortwave oscillators. The first figure shows the structure of the entire machine, and the second figure is its circuit diagram. The maximum capacity of the tuning capacitor is 16-20 unfd. It is quite suitable to use three ordinary small capacitors. The oscillator tube can be either a No. 71 tube (5v.) or a No. 45 tube (2.5v.). The .o5ufd bypass capacitor in the filament circuit must be inserted. If it is not inserted, the vacuum tube will inevitably burn out.

For amplitude modulation, the secondary line of the push-pull audio frequency transformer is inserted into the plate circuit, and a buzzer and telegraph key are connected to one end of the primary line, and the other end is connected to the output of the audio frequency two-stage amplifier to perform amplitude modulation. In this way, it is possible to transmit telegraph or telephone without using a separate vacuum tube. The B voltage is supplied at 150-200V.

The above device is not a problem if it is only used for the study of ordinary oscillators. However, if it is actually used for communication with the outside world, it cannot be used because its oscillation frequency is extremely prone to change, often leading to a state where it cannot be received. To prevent this, the oscillation method should be changed to push-pull. The third figure shows its structure, and its circuit is shown in the fourth figure. The vacuum tube is still the former one, while the capacitor and others are slightly different from the former one. The variable capacitor can be a dual-gang with five or seven plates. It is better to use thick copper wire for the coil.

L1 diameter 6 inches 1 turn

L2 diameter 1 inch 4 turns

Choke diameter 1 inch 18 turns

When performing amplitude modulation, use the constant current amplitude modulation method. According to experiments, this machine can reach a distance of about K.M. without using an antenna. Whether the transmitter is oscillating can be determined by using a coil of the same size as the tuning coil to connect an annual red lamp to resonate with the coil of the transmitter. If the transmitter is oscillating, the annual red lamp will light up; if it is not oscillating, it will not light up.

Improvement of High-Frequency Coils 156

— Qing Jian

The coil shown in the figure is made by improving the winding method of the antenna coil and the tuning coil. As shown in the figure, the tuning coil 2 is wound on the insulating cylinder 1. However, when winding, the two ends of 2, that is, the grid section 2' and the ground section 2", must be tightly wound, and the central section 2" must be wound especially sparsely. Also, at the joint 2', the antenna coil and the coil of 2 are alternately wound for five to seven-fourths of a turn. The antenna coil is not grounded. In the figure, 4 is the regenerative coil. If 2 and 3 are wound alternately, it is easy to cause capacitive coupling. Therefore, the number of antenna coil turns can be reduced. Also, because the center of the tuning coil is wound sparsely, the distributed capacitance between the windings can be reduced. This improved winding method is quite applicable.

Self-Generating Radio 157

— Juan

As shown in the figure, a vacuum tube radio is installed in a box, and a lever-type motor (3) with a handle (6) is also installed in the same box. Its output rotary shaft (8) is connected to a magnet generator (4), and the electricity generated by this generator is supplied to the radio (2). The so-called motor (3) here is just like the motor used in a gramophone. By rotating the handle, considerable power is stored. The previous radios were either mains-powered or battery-powered. The former is not easy to use if there is no power line or during a power outage, and the latter is quite expensive and heavy. Both have inconveniences, but this self-generating radio does not have the above inconveniences and can be used everywhere. (From Wireless and Experiment Magazine)

Simple Superheterodyne Three-Tube Radio (Continued from Issue 138) 158

— Cao Runsheng

(I) Simple Circuit: The circuit of this machine is extremely simple, using three of the 30 vacuum tubes that every researcher has. The circuit is similar to that of ordinary three-tube machines, so it is very suitable for beginners to assemble.

(II) High Selectivity: This machine is a superheterodyne, so its selectivity is very good. All radio stations in Shanghai can be completely distinguished without any mixing.

(III) High Sensitivity: The sensitivity of this machine is quite excellent. Although it only has three tubes, all radio stations in Shanghai can be listened to in the loudspeaker without any omission. The volume is slightly lower than that of ordinary tube machines.

In summary, this machine is well worth a try, and the cost is minimal. You can try out the superheterodyne circuit and get a practical radio. Why not do it? The method of making the whole machine is recorded below:

LL1 is a high-frequency transformer. It can be wound on a large spiderweb board with 26-gauge wire: L1 10 turns, L 10 turns.

Use a thin wooden stick to string the coil in the middle, separated by a copper sheet. Each coil is one inch away from the copper sheet. This is the end of the reading. When using, the lower end of the copper sheet can be folded into a right angle and installed on the bottom plate. The bottom plate is then grounded (see figure).

Prepare all the other parts and then you can start assembling.

L2L3 These two coils are the intermediate frequency transformer. The quality of this component really affects the performance of the whole machine, so do not be sloppy when manufacturing it. Use wood to turn two wooden cores of the same size (dimensions as shown in the figure), and then wind 800 turns of 26-gauge single-strand wire on each wooden core. Those who have assembled one or two vacuum tube radios will not fail. However, be very careful when calibrating. The most important thing is that when calibrating C2C3 to the loudest sound, do not move them anymore, and make the short-wave and long-wave radio stations have an average volume. Only then is the position of C2 and C3 correct. In normal use, turn CC1 with both hands at the same time. The numbers on the dials of C and C1 are approximately ten degrees apart. If you can use a dual-gang capacitor, the adjustment can be more convenient, but you must use small padding capacitors, and the calibration is also not easy, so a single one is used here. (The End)

Supply of Voltages to the Various Electrodes of a Vacuum Tube 159

— Guan Tingzhen

(I) Filament or Heater

Although vacuum tubes allow for slight changes in the voltage and current of the filament or heater during design, the specified values must be used for high efficiency. If the voltage used is lower than specified, the temperature of the cathode will also be low, resulting in limiting the emission of electrons, making the work of the vacuum tube unsuitable, and thus reducing its life. If the voltage used is higher than specified, the substances on the cathode will easily evaporate, which can also reduce its life. Therefore, to maintain the perfection of the vacuum tube, the voltage of the filament or heater must be checked with a voltmeter when the radio is turned on. If the filaments are connected in series, an ammeter can be connected in the filament circuit to correct its current.

The filament or heater can be supplied with direct current (battery or DC power supply) or alternating current. Usually, when using direct current, a resistor (variable or fixed) can be used to adjust the voltage. When using alternating current, a step-down transformer can be used to supply the voltage of the filament or heater. However, for radios that use both AC and DC, the filaments are connected in series with a step-down resistor, which can be directly plugged into the power line.

If the direct current filament or heater is supplied with dry batteries, a variable resistor should be connected in series between the filament and the battery to control the change in the battery. It is best to install an accurate voltmeter or milliampere meter in the radio so that the filament of the vacuum tube can obtain a specified voltage. The voltage of the battery often changes when it is stopped, so using a resistor can also serve as a switch to stop it. If sometimes using storage batteries or air batteries or DC power supplies, appropriate fixed resistors can be used. It is best to use a voltmeter or ammeter to calibrate for the first time. If the vacuum tube uses two volts, a storage battery can be directly connected in series. If the vacuum tube uses 6.3 volts, a 6-volt storage battery can be directly connected in series without using a resistor.

The size of the filament or heater resistance in parallel can be calculated using Ohm's law:

If the radio uses three No. 32 tubes, two No. 30 tubes, and two No. 31 tubes connected to dry batteries, then the series resistance is equal to 3 volts (using two dry batteries in series) minus 2 volts (the specified voltage of the vacuum tube) divided by 0.56 amperes (the sum of 5xo.o6o amperes and 2xo.i3o amperes). The answer is approximately 1.8 ohms, so resistors of 2 to 3 ohms can also be used, but it is best to purchase resistors with a larger number of ohms, because most of the electrical power is consumed on the resistor. If resistors with a larger number of ohms are used, they will not overheat and be damaged. The calculation of electrical power (unit: watt) is: the sum of the filament current multiplied by the voltage drop of the resistor, which is 6 watts. Since the number of watts is so small, general commercial resistors can be used. (To be continued)

Regulations for Submissions to This Publication 160

1. This publication is a weekly, published every Saturday.

2. The purpose of this publication is to contribute modestly to China's backward and impoverished academic and publishing circles with a rigorous attitude from the aspects of "research," "introduction," and "criticism."

3. This publication welcomes external submissions on the following topics: (A) personal reading experiences, (B) research on Chinese and foreign writers, (C) summaries of famous Chinese and foreign works, (D) introductions and critiques of books and newspapers, (E) news from cultural circles in various regions.

4. Submissions of drawings and woodcuts related to reading and the publishing industry are especially welcome.

5. Submissions should preferably be no more than 2,000 characters in length.

6. Please indicate your name and mailing address on submissions.

7. Submissions will not be returned, regardless of whether they are published. However, this does not apply to those who include a self-addressed stamped envelope.

8. Once a submission is published, a modest payment of two to four yuan per thousand characters will be offered.

9. Please send submissions to No. 234, Avenue Edward VII, Shanghai.

Special Publication for the 20th Anniversary of Ginling Women's Arts and Science College

Foreword 161

Time flies, and this school has been established for twenty years. In the past twenty years, from imitating pioneers and building with difficulty, it has gradually reached its present scale. Whether this school has made considerable contributions to women's higher education can be generally understood through its annual development and growth. However, reviewing the past is a strategy for the future, especially given the country's difficulties. This school seeks to adapt to the needs of the times and must continue to seek progress. Therefore, it briefly describes the current situation and future plans, seeking guidance from those who are knowledgeable, which is also the school's long-cherished wish.

Higher education is related to the rise and fall of national culture and bears a heavy responsibility. It is definitely not something that can be perfected by the wisdom of a few people. This school has always received enthusiastic care and assistance from people in society. On the occasion of its twentieth anniversary, it presents a brief overview, which, in addition to being included in the school's journal, is also briefly presented in this space. It is deeply grateful for the encouraging words given by the administrative officers and those enthusiastic about education. It hereby expresses its gratitude and hopes that people in society will continue to provide assistance and guidance with their usual enthusiasm, which would not only be the school's good fortune but also the nation's blessing.

Progress Over Twenty Years 162

This school was established in 1915. Time flies, and twenty years have passed. The past is like yesterday, and the annual growth and expansion are still vivid in my mind. On the occasion of this twentieth anniversary, I will recount a few things to inspire future development. For the sake of clarity, I have divided the narrative into three periods, as described below.

First Period – The Founding Period – 1915 to 1921

The Motivation for Founding Women's education in China, run by churches, began quite early. Church girls' schools in Ningbo, Zhenjiang, Jiujiang, Nanjing, and other places had a history of thirty or forty years by the early Republic of China. Over time, the content also became more comprehensive. Therefore, in the summer of 1913, the principals of various church girls' middle schools along the lower reaches of the Yangtze River gathered to discuss further steps for women's education, based on two reasons. One was for the sake of graduation and further education, and the other was to alleviate the lack of teachers. The former was because there was no women's university in the country at that time, and ordinary universities were not open to women. Therefore, if female middle school graduates did not go abroad, they had no place to further their education. However, the cost of going abroad was very high, and only those from wealthy families could afford it. Moreover, middle school graduates were still young, and once they left home and went abroad, their understanding of the domestic situation was not yet clear, which was not the best option. Regarding the latter, each girls' school wanted to hire female teachers who had graduated from university, but there were no institutions in the country to train them, and women who returned from studying abroad were extremely rare and not easy to find. Due to the above two reasons, a proposal was made for further progress: the motivation to establish a women's university.

Preparations After the principals of various girls' middle schools made the proposal, they sought the consent of various churches, because at that time the standards and expectations for the proposed women's university were extremely high, and it was known that it could not be managed with the financial and human resources of one church alone. Subsequently, the Presbyterian Church, the Methodist Episcopal Church, the Methodist Church, the Baptist Church, the Christian Church, and other five denominations agreed. In November of that year, directors were elected and a board of directors was established. Therefore, this association commemorates November as the anniversary of its establishment because the board of directors was formed in that month. After the board of directors was established, Nanjing was chosen as the location for the school, and the school was named Ginling Women's University. Mrs. Lawrence Thurston was elected as president and was responsible for the preparations. Mrs. Thurston had the talent to run a school, and she planned and coordinated in various ways. Finally, preparations were completed in 1915, and enrollment began. Classes officially started in September of that year.

Opening Situation At the beginning of its opening, the scale was extremely small. At that time, the school building had not yet been built, and the Li family's residence in Embroidery Lane was rented. There were only nine students, coming from four provinces, who had graduated from six girls' middle schools. The number of faculty and staff was also nine, which was equal. Except for two people who held concurrent positions, the rest were full-time. It can be seen that the leaders did not neglect their studies because of the small number of students. This spirit was maintained throughout. The annual operating cost was 10,500 yuan, and the equipment was worth 3,772 yuan. Apart from the Encyclopedia Britannica, there were no other reference books.

Growth Situation In 1916, the second class of students was recruited, adding another nine students. Because one student from the first class dropped out, the total number of students in both classes was only seventeen. By the fourth year of operation, there were four classes of students, but the number was still only fifty-two. However, compared to the initial opening, the scope had increased, and there were twenty-three faculty and staff members. The London Missionary Society, the Anglican Church Missionary Society, and the United Methodist Church also joined in cooperation. Smith College in the United States also recognized this school as a sister school, and each year students and alumni of that school were responsible for a portion of the funding. Therefore, the foundation of this school became more solid at this time.

First Graduation In the summer of 1919, this school held its first graduation ceremony. There were only five graduates, and they were recognized by the State University of New York, which awarded them Bachelor of Arts degrees. Among the five graduates, two became teachers in national schools, two became teachers in church middle schools, and the other went to an American medical university to study medicine.

Second Period – The Expansion Period – 1921 to 1927

Purchasing Land and Building School Buildings During the years of 1920 and 1921, the seven Associated Women's Colleges in China, Japan, and India, run by various American churches, had a considerable foundation. In order to seek further progress, a major fundraising campaign was held to build school buildings. The alumnae of Smith College also helped with fundraising. Therefore, this school obtained a large amount of construction funds, purchased land in Taowu Valley, hired workers and materials, and started construction. By 1923, the Main Building, the Arts Building, the Science Building, and dormitories were gradually completed. The total cost of the land and construction was more than 900,000 silver dollars. In the autumn of that year, the school moved into the new campus. With more spacious buildings, the number of applicants increased day by day.

Enriching Content After moving into the new campus, because the construction aspect could be temporarily put on hold, efforts were made to enrich the content. In addition to equipment such as books and instruments, professors were hired, academic programs were added, and students were required to choose a major and minor department. Also, because the school site was moved to Taowu Valley, close to the University of Nanking, the two universities allowed students to cross-register for advanced courses in order to gain more knowledge.

Merger of the Women's Physical Education Teachers' School The Women's Physical Education Teachers' School, run by the National Association of the Young Women's Christian Association of Shanghai, enrolled high school graduates for two years of physical education training. In order to improve the students' level, the school was merged into the Physical Education Department of this school in 1925.

Establishment of an Affiliated Middle School In the autumn of 1924, because most of the graduates of the Education Department of this school served as teachers in various middle schools, in order to provide them with teaching experience and increase their service efficiency, a class of affiliated experimental middle school was established. This was the beginning of the current senior affiliated middle school.

Rockefeller Foundation Grant The Rockefeller Foundation Medical Committee found that the content of natural sciences in this school had reached a considerable level, so it gave an annual grant to encourage it.

Third Period – The Restructuring Period – 1927 to Present

Re-election of the President In 1927, after the National Government moved to Nanjing, the University Council stipulated that the president of a university must be a Chinese citizen. Therefore, Mrs. Lawrence Thurston, the president of this school, resigned from the board of directors and requested that a Chinese citizen be re-elected to succeed her, in order to show obedience to government laws. The board of directors appreciated her aspirations and re-elected Dr. Wu Yifang as president. Dr. Wu was a graduate of the first class of this school, had served as the director of the English Department of the National Beijing Women's Higher Normal School for three years, and had studied in the United States for six years. She took office in the autumn of 1928.

Change of School Name After the promulgation of the University Organization Law, this school prepared for registration in accordance with this law and changed its name to Private Ginling Women's Arts and Science College in accordance with the organization law. It applied to the Ministry of Education for registration and was formally approved in the winter of 1930.

Change of the Physical Education Simple Course to a Specialized Course This school recognized the shortage of physical education teachers in primary and secondary schools, so in the autumn of 1929, it established a class of physical education simple course, enrolling high school graduates and providing them with one year of physical education training. They graduated in the summer of 1930 and were almost all hired by various primary and secondary schools. However, many graduates were willing to receive another year of training, so starting in the autumn of 1930, the physical education specialized course was changed to a two-year program. There have already been three classes of graduates, and because there is a great need in society, it continues to be offered to this day.

Change of the Affiliated Experimental Middle School to a Senior Middle School The Affiliated Experimental Middle School had been established since 1924, and there was only one class, which was not expanded. In 1932, seeing the need for additional girls' high schools in the capital, the existing experimental middle school was changed into a purely girls' senior middle school. It was registered with the Nanjing Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in May 1933, and the Ministry of Education also approved the record. The school name was changed to the Affiliated Senior Middle School of this school.

New Buildings of This School The new buildings of this school can be divided into the affiliated middle school and the university. (A) For the affiliated middle school, a three-story dormitory building was built. This was donated by Mrs. Sun Yat-sen, Mrs. Kong Xiangxi, and Mrs. Chiang Kai-shek to commemorate their mothers, expressing filial piety and benefiting students, which is truly admirable. (B) For the university, because when the school buildings were built before, there was still some remaining funds, which were not enough to build two large buildings at that time, so they were temporarily deposited in the bank to generate interest. In 1932, it was decided to withdraw the principal and interest for construction to complete the planned project. The completion ceremony was held at this time last year. The building on the north side is used as a library and office, and the building on the south side is used as a auditorium and music room.

The above points are only a general description of the progress of this school over the past twenty years. Due to space limitations, it is not possible to present them in detail. However, there is one more point that can be mentioned: starting from the previous year, the Ministry of Education has been providing subsidies to excellent private colleges and universities. This school receives a subsidy of more than 10,000 yuan per year. Although the amount is not large, it is worth noting that the authorities are able to provide incentives to excellent private schools.

The Current Situation and Characteristics of This School 163

Sources of Students The number of women's higher education institutions in our country is very small. In the north, there is only the Women's College of Arts and Sciences of National Peking University, and in the south, there is only the Hwa Nan Women's College of Fujou. As for the central region, there is only this school. Therefore, judging from the provinces of the current students enrolled in this school, there are Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Sichuan, Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, Hebei, Shanxi, Liaoning, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou, and Nanyang, covering almost the entire country. In terms of the middle schools from which they graduated, there are as many as eighty schools, which is quite extensive.

Value of Equipment The equipment of this school, including school buildings, books, instruments, utensils, and land, has cost more than 1.5 million yuan. Compared with the time of establishment, it is almost 500 times greater.

Departments and Programs This school currently has two departments: arts and sciences. The departments established in each department are listed separately below.

Arts Department Major Departments: Chinese Literature, English Literature, History, Philosophy, Sociology, Music, Physical Education. The Physical Education Department has an affiliated Physical Education Specialized Course. Minor Departments: Psychology, Education. The Education Department has an affiliated Senior High School.

Science Department Major Departments: Biology, Chemistry, Mathematics and Physics, Geography

Minor Departments: Hygiene

Richness of Academic Programs According to a recent survey by the Christian Education Association, among the thirteen Christian universities in the country, the number of students at this school is often ranked tenth or eleventh, but the total number of teaching hours per semester is ranked fifth or sixth. This shows the richness of the academic programs offered by this school.

Accuracy of Course Offerings The courses offered by this school are based on the needs of the students. For example, if the majority of graduates will be middle school teachers, then education is offered as a minor to clarify the principles of education and teaching methods. An affiliated middle school is also established to provide practical teaching and gain more experience. Each science department also offers special education methods to learn how to collect specimens, purchase instruments, and adopt textbooks. Also, in recent years, social construction has been emphasized. Because women are quiet and suitable for social work, the Sociology Department, in addition to guiding majors in conducting various field investigations, also has a Social Service Center to help students understand the living conditions of nearby farmers and workers and study and solve their difficult problems. If a course is requested by five or more students, efforts are made to open a class for them.

Attention to Lower-Level Students The basic courses such as Chinese and English for first- and second-year students are divided into small groups for teaching, so that it is easier to provide separate guidance, consolidate their foundation, and easily improve their grades. According to previous graduates who entered graduate schools, they are often able to obtain considerable honors. The only female student who was admitted to study in the UK with the Boxer Indemnity Scholarship two years ago was also a graduate of this school. This is related to the practical training of basic courses given to them at the beginning of their enrollment.

Research Atmosphere The atmosphere of academic research among the teachers and students of this school is strong. Various academic societies are able to be realistic and seek truth from facts. For example, during the recent Italian-Ethiopian War, the Geographical Society proposed a study of the geography of Italy and Ethiopia, so that students interested in geography could study, report, and discuss. Professors also publish books according to the needs of the academic community, such as gymnastics and dance by the Physical Education Department, middle school mathematics by Ms. Lu, and zoology by Dr. Li.

Training Beyond Knowledge This school upholds the principle that education is life and emphasizes the balanced development of students in all aspects, in order to cultivate their whole personality and talents. A few points are briefly described below.

1. Physical Fitness Training Physical and fitness examinations are conducted every autumn when school starts. The physical examination is conducted by the school doctor. Those who are not healthy are given special guidance or treatment. The fitness examination is conducted by the Physical Education Department. The results of the examination are classified into intense, moderate, and restricted physical education classes to provide appropriate training, improve their health. They are also taught a course on hygiene, and then tested again in the spring to see if there has been any progress.

2. Leadership Training Various organizations and regulations are in place for academic and extracurricular activities, so as to train students to gain experience in handling affairs, have methods to deal with or solve problems, develop a spirit of cooperation and responsibility, and serve society after graduation. In addition to the students themselves feeling the benefits of this training, those who work with them also praise it.

3. Cultivation of Service Habits What students learn is preparation for the future. However, if they only care about increasing their personal knowledge and do not contact the outside world, they often do not understand the needs of society or develop the drawbacks of selfishness. Therefore, students of this school, in their spare time, pay attention to cultivating the habit of practical service. A few examples are briefly cited to clarify this.

First, the Student YWCA founded the Peiyou Primary School, which was established from the second year of the school's opening and has not been interrupted. It has also been able to improve according to the needs of the environment. Recently, because a municipal primary school has been established not far from the school, it has been changed to the Yifan Women's Home Economics School this autumn, teaching older female students domestic knowledge.

Second, in 1931, during the great flood in the Yangtze River, the government conducted a survey of the entire disaster area to distribute relief funds according to the severity of the disaster. When the survey forms from various counties were all sent in, the survey committee lacked people to organize and count them. When the students of this school learned of this, they automatically donated their time to assist in the organization work every night for more than a month before it was completed.

Homelike Life with Group Organization Each dormitory of this school has a recreation room and a dining room, so that the roommates have a place to gather, like family members chatting. As for the bedrooms, the students sweep themselves and train in simple and clean living. Teachers get along with students like sisters in their spare time. Students like to ask teachers to be advisors for any organization they have, and teachers gladly participate, so the relationship between teachers and students is like a family, and there is even a sister class organization among students. This phenomenon is possible because most of the teachers and students of this school live on campus.

The above points are only a rough description of the current situation of this school or a brief review of the past. The teachers and staff of this school work hard and do not care about the salary. Graduates also go to poor and remote areas, such as the newly recovered bandit areas of Lichuan, Jiangxi, and bury themselves in work. This spirit of sacrifice is truly commendable.

Current Status Survey of Graduates 164

In 1919, this school held its first graduation, with only five graduates. Since then, there has been a graduation every year. This summer, it has reached the seventeenth graduation. They serve society with dedication and responsibility and have gained the trust of people in society. Therefore, during this period of serious employment problems, students of this school are still in high demand. According to the statistics of the Career Services Office, in the past three years, the number of people who have been hired by this school has exceeded the number of graduates by about three times, which shows the trust of people in society in the graduates of this school, which is very gratifying. As for those who seek further education, the number exceeds a quarter of all graduates. In terms of this number, there are not many to see in the country. Special "Crab" Publication of "Chunqiu"

Tidbits 183

— (Huang Lian)

One by one, large, fat crabs are displayed in baskets in front of stores. The four characters "Fresh Lake Crab" arouse the appetite of the rich! They sting the hearts of the poor!

"When the crabs are fat, you must remember, the navel is round in September, the tip in October!" In front of the stores selling crabs, there is quarreling over the roundness and tip of the navel! There is fighting over the size! … Mr. Chen's dozens of baskets of lake crabs are all sold out in the midst of a clamor.

Thus, one day, two days, …, it is like this every day, watching the crab buyers hand silver coins one by one to the clerk, without the slightest stinginess!

Hey! Crab eaters! Now I will tell you an important matter, that is, the 20,000,000 disaster victims in various disaster areas are exposed to the wind and dew, and urgently await our relief!

Saving the money for one crab is enough to save a disaster victim's life! With the utmost sincerity, Huang Lian makes a plea on behalf of the 20,000,000 disaster victims in the country!

Crab People 184

— Zhu Ying

The autumn wind rises, and the sideways walking gentlemen gradually become chesty and fat. It's precisely the right time for scholars to compose poems about chrysanthemums while enjoying a good drink. It's not necessarily limited to scholars and elegant gentlemen; even common laborers and vulgar fellows, city monks and uncouth men, all have the means to buy five premium crabs. Returning home, they face their yellow-faced wives and munch on them for a while.

Indeed, the taste of crabs is delicious, something everyone acknowledges. But I wonder how many crab eaters know about the suffering in the lives of crab catchers. The author grew up in a water town and has seen the lives of crab catchers since childhood. Crab catching relies entirely on crab traps made of woven bamboo. Tall and short bamboo fences are planted haphazardly in the river, intermittently connecting the east bank to the west bank, forming a formation. Each crab weir, when set up, generally costs at least one hundred yuan or more at current prices, and annual repairs cost at least twenty yuan. Each crab weir lasts for at most ten years. As for the harvest, during the nine or ten months of the fishing season, a good one might yield close to two hundred yuan, while a poor year might only bring in about one hundred yuan. In the crab market, the income seems quite considerable, but what else can be obtained after the crab season? All that's left are mud shrimp and small crucian carp, things that don't fetch much money. Therefore, the lives of "crab people" are just like those of ordinary farmers, struggling in poverty and destitution year after year.

Crab catching is always done at night. Dim yellow lights hanging on the crab weirs tell you that the "crab people" are active. In that dim yellow light, armor-clad generals, attracted to the light, climb the weirs and become prey for the crab catchers. This scene might be considered poetic and artistic by young gentlemen in ivory towers, but the crab people are all complaining and blaming fate, regretting making a living this way, certain that they will starve to death one day. Because in Shanghai, a large crab costs one yuan, while at the crab catcher's place, one yuan can buy at least three catties or more.

Crab Catching Methods 185

— Cheng Ming

Time flies so fast; in the blink of an eye, it's already late autumn again. In the alleys and streets, you can hear the calls of "Want to buy crabs?" everywhere. This reminds us of the fun we had catching crabs in our childhood.

Catching crabs: How do you catch them? According to the methods in my eastern hometown, there are about three kinds, such as "weir crabs," "weir crabs," and "net crabs." Among these three methods, "weir crabs" are considered the most convenient and easiest to catch.

The weir crab method only requires using a net barrier to cut across the river port to catch crabs. The net barrier is made of thick hemp thread, woven into a flat net about three feet wide and twenty feet long. On the lower edge of the net, more than ten three-inch long, three- or four-tenths of an inch thick iron bars are fastened. Then, using a bamboo pole about twelve or thirteen feet long, the net barrier is lifted to the riverbank opposite the river port. When the bamboo pole is pulled back, the net barrier will sink to the bottom of the river. The upper end of the net barrier near the body is propped up with a bamboo chopstick, which is inserted into the mud on the riverbank. An oil lamp must also be placed next to the net's end because crab fishing must be done between 8 PM and 12 AM. When the crabs see the light, they will throw themselves into the net. If the upper end of the net barrier moves slightly, the net barrier is pulled up, and one by one, the large crabs, trapped in the mesh, like a string of beads, can be obtained effortlessly, five or six or seven or eight at a time. The amount of crabs caught depends on the coldness of the weather. The colder the weather, the more crabs are caught. Sometimes, dozens can be caught continuously every hour, which is very interesting! However, the river port for weir crabs must be a clear water river. There are very few in tidal rivers, and because they are washed by the tide, net barriers cannot be used. Crab nets can only be used to rake for crabs, or bamboo weirs can be used to weir crabs. Therefore, catching crabs in tidal rivers is not easy.

Weir crabs are probably monopolistic. One-inch thick, ten-foot-long pieces of mao bamboo are woven into a bamboo fence-like long curtain, which is cut across the heart of the river. The lower end of the bamboo pieces is inserted into the bottom of the river, and the two ends are tied to wooden stakes on both banks with thick hemp ropes. Another bamboo weir, three or four feet square and ten or more feet high, is made and firmly leaned against the bamboo curtain. It must be built sturdily so that the crabs swimming back and forth in the river can climb to the top of the bamboo curtain and fall into the bamboo weir, where a net can be used to scoop them up. Using this method to catch crabs can sometimes yield more than weir crabs because it uses monopolistic means to catch them, truly "wiping them out in one fell swoop."

Net crabs also have two kinds. One is "carrying" (two people dragging) net crab catching, using a large net with the tips of the four corners fastened with hemp ropes. One end of the net corner is tied to wooden stakes on both banks of the river, and the ropes at the other two ends are thrown onto the bridge railing. Three people must keep watch, pulling the net about every five minutes. If there are fish and crabs in the net, another person uses a net to scoop them up. If there is no bridge on the river, then two people have to stand on both banks to drag the net, which seems very strenuous.

Another kind is raking for crabs, using a square net made of bamboo heads, which is lowered into the river to rake. This method is convenient and can be used to catch crabs anywhere, but it is not suitable for catching crabs in deep river ports. Larger lakes can use this method to catch crabs.

Sideways Walking 186

— Juan Yin

Understanding Crabs 187

— Yan BOGuang

Yellow chrysanthemums are blooming, and maple leaves are dyed with rouge. It is the time for holding crabs, drinking wine, appreciating chrysanthemums, and composing poetry. However, although crabs are delicious, they contain "grinding his life" essence, which can destroy a person's health. Moreover, they are too cold and can easily cause illness if eaten improperly.

There are river crabs and lake crabs. Lake crabs have tender and fresh meat, while river crabs have lean and bland meat. Every place that sells crabs in the market hangs a sign saying "Fresh Large Lake Crabs." Some even hang signs saying "Yangcheng Lake Crabs" to attract customers. But how many of them are real Yangcheng Lake crabs? If gourmets want to recognize the genuine Yangcheng Lake crabs, it is very easy. The crab's back is blue, the claws are golden, the hairs are yellow, and when placed on a gilded table, the crab's abdomen can walk sideways away from the table. This is powerful proof. When I worked in Wumen for three years, an old gourmet told me this, saying: "In Suzhou, you can't eat real Yangcheng Lake crabs; they are all imitations from Pingwang Yingduli Lake." So where did the Yangcheng Lake crabs go? They went to Shanghai to sell for a good price.

Poisonous crabs are: those with only one claw, one eye, two eyes facing each other, six or four feet, hair under the abdomen, bones in the abdomen, stars on the back, and red eyes. Eating the above can easily cause poisoning. Winter melon juice, perilla juice, garlic juice, fermented soybean juice, and reed root juice can all detoxify crab poison.

Crabs can cause wind. People with wind diseases should not eat them. Crabs and persimmons are incompatible and should never be eaten together. Eating them together can cause cholera.

Since crabs have so many harms, we cannot help but eat them because they are delicious. We can only be extra careful when choosing them. When we bring them home, we wash them clean with a clean water brush, embed a slice of fresh ginger and several grains of salt in the navel, and put a handful of perilla leaves and water into the pot (available at Chinese medicine stores). After the crabs are tied up, they are placed on top of the perilla leaves and boiled. Simmer briefly, and eat with more ginger. Never eat it with Shi Guogong's medicine!

There is a saying that crabs have nine pointed parts and ten round parts, but in late September and early October of the lunar calendar, each has its own charm, with fat intestines and full roe, which can be enjoyed greatly. People with cold stomachs should eat a bowl of longan soup after eating crabs to avoid stomach pain and abdominal pain.

Crab Recipes 188

— (Hong Yang)

Dry-Steamed Crab Meat and Roe: The method is to use freshwater crabs weighing four or five taels each, wash them clean, and place them in a steamer to heat. Remove the crab meat and crab roe and crab oil. When peeling, be sure not to mix the roe and oil into the crab meat, and place them separately. After peeling, take a large basin, place the crab meat on the bottom of the basin, and spread the crab legs and claws on top, topping it off with crab oil. Slightly pour in aged wine, cover with a sea bowl, and steam over high heat. Remove immediately, pour two spoons of minced scallions and boiling lard on top of the crab meat, and the dry-steamed crab meat and roe is complete. When eating, be sure to mix in the prepared ginger mince and sugar vinegar while it is hot, so that the taste is fresh and has a true flavor.

Crab Omelet: Crab omelet is a strong flavor in crab dishes. The method is to wash the large crab shell, leaving the two teeth of the shell connecting the crab bag in the center of the shell edge. Put the peeled crab meat, crab roe, and minced fatty meat into the shell, level with the shell, and spread meat crumbs on top of the meat crumbs. Coat the surface with egg mixed with flour, sear until golden brown in boiling oil, add aged wine, soy sauce, white sugar and water over the top, and cook over high heat until the soup becomes thick, the flavor is extremely strong and beautiful. The most important thing is to mix some aged wine, soy sauce, and white sugar into the batter, and it is also good to add a little minced green onion and ginger, but do not add vinegar and salt, and the seasoning must be accurate, not too salty or too sweet.

Crab Soup: Crab soup is a type of soup. The method is to briefly fry crab meat in lard, add wine, soy sauce, minced green onion and ginger, and water. Cook it into a soup, and after it boils for five or six minutes, add yellow flour to make a thick soup. When it boils, take it up, and the crab soup is complete. If you like sour, you can add a little rice vinegar, but it is best not to add it.

Gold Inlaid Jade: Gold Inlaid Jade is made with crab roe and crab oil. The method is to put crab roe and crab oil in a lard pot and fry it. Immediately add wine, soy sauce, and white sugar, and remove it immediately after it boils. Crab oil is easy to dissolve, so the lard must be extremely boiling. After putting it in the pot, it must be quickly removed, otherwise the crab oil will dissolve into the lard.

Sichuan Large Feet: Sichuan Large Feet is made with the meat of crab legs and claws. First, boil them in chicken soup, pour in the crab meat, and add wine to remove the fishy taste after boiling. Then add salt and remove from the pot and eat. It is clear, rich, fresh, and without any oil, making it a delicacy in clear soup.

Fried Crab Meat Noodles: Mix the peeled crab meat with a little aged wine and salt, and then mix in minced fresh meat. Wrap it in tofu skin into a long shape, coat it with egg mixed with flour, and fry it in lard. When the egg noodles turn yellow, you can dip it in vinegar and eat it. It is crispy and delicious.

Crab Meat Cabbage Heart: Take the heart of green vegetables, cut it into strips about an inch long, and put it in a lard pot to stir-fry. When the cabbage heart is about to soften, add crab meat and a little chicken soup and cook until the vegetables are soft. Add wine and salt and cook until the soup is thick. Take it out to eat. The taste of the cabbage heart is better than that of the crab meat, but when cooking this, do not cover the pot, because the vegetables will turn yellow after covering, and the clear aroma of the vegetables will be completely lost. If you do not cover it, the color will be green and the true flavor of the vegetables can be preserved. If there is no chicken soup, you can add water and mix in monosodium glutamate, which is also very delicious.

There are other crab recipes, but due to space limitations, I cannot say more, but to cook crabs, you must use good aged wine to remove the fishy taste of the crabs. This is the most important thing.

How to Eat Crabs 189

— (Ying Dai)

Crab is indeed a very delicious thing among aquatic foods. Once autumn arrives, in addition to the streets being filled with crab stalls, the people selling along the streets carry loads, open their throats, and shout "Crabs! Crabs!..." And then people will once again experience the craze for eating crabs. There are also thresholds for eating crabs. If you eat them without knowing the proper way, you will lose the delicious taste.

First, we must also look at the season when eating crabs. In early autumn, crabs are just coming onto the market, and nineteen out of ten are so thin that they have no meat. When cooked, they are just a bag of water, not only not fresh but also have a bitter taste. Strictly speaking, crabs only become fat and strong when the west wind rises. Around the beginning of last month of the lunar calendar is the best time to eat crabs. In September of the lunar calendar, female crabs are probably better than male crabs, and in October, male crabs are better. Therefore, there is a saying "Nine female and ten male," which we can take as a guide to eating crabs.

The most refreshing way to eat crabs is of course to use what Shanghai people call "a large boiled crab," which is to cook the crab with clean water and eat it with soy sauce. However, even "a large boiled crab" has its own thresholds. Eating the crabs as soon as they come out of the water is of course the freshest. Because we buy so many that we can't finish them all at once, we inevitably raise them for a day or two, but we can't keep them for too long, because they will become thin if kept for too long. When cooking, use cold water. If you use warm water, the crab legs will fall off. The process should not be too long or too short. If it is too long, the crab meat will become old; if it is too short, it will not be cooked through. When you open the pot and see cracks in the crab's back, you're done. Eat "large boiled crabs" while they are hot. It is best to eat them as soon as they are taken out of the pot. Use high-quality natural soy sauce. Some people think that crabs are very cold, so they put ginger, pepper, and other things in the soy sauce. Some people take a few sips of wine after eating crabs, and some people put perilla, ginger, and other things in the pot when cooking them to remove the cold air.

There are many ways to eat crabs. In addition to "large boiled crabs," you can also peel the meat from "large boiled crabs" and use lard, soy sauce, and other seasonings to stir-fry crab meat. If you put more in crab meat soup, it becomes crab soup. In addition, crab stewed eggs, crab scrambled eggs, crab meat shreds, crab meat balls, crab fried tofu, crab fried bean curd sheets, etc., are too many to list. They are all made with peeled crab meat. However, we must not forget one thing, which is that when cooking things with crab meat, you should probably put some of the soup from the beginning of cooking the crab in it after filtering it, which will make it extra delicious.

In addition, people who are particular about eating peel a lot of crab meat between September and October and put it in a pot to cook with lard, called crab pork fat. After freezing, it can be stored for a long time without spoiling. When the weather is cold in the middle of winter and there are no crabs on the market, put some crab pork fat in the soup or dishes. It is not only very delicious but also has a crab flavor. I believe people who eat crabs may want to cook some crab pork fat and store it.

Little Knowledge

Common Sense About Holding Crabs 190

— Tian Xu WOSheng

Crab should not be eaten with persimmons or jingjie (Nepeta tenuifolia), which all old people know, but in new foods, there are often reactions that cause poisoning. The wife of Xiao Die, Xian Jun, used to eat crab with brandy without noticing anything at first. After a few hours, she had excruciating abdominal pain and vomited to relieve it. The wife of the second Die once ate crab with wine and had the same symptoms. I didn't believe it at first, so I tried it myself. It was very strange. In the middle of the night, I suddenly woke up with excruciating intestinal pain. Vomiting medicine was ineffective. My intestines were rumbling, and my abdominal wall bulged out like a fist. I then took diluted hydrochloric acid and rhubarb wine. To get to the bottom of it, I first read in the herbal classics that Tao Hongjing said: "Crabs before the frost are poisonous, which is caused by eating water solanum (i.e., belladonna in Western medicine). If people are poisoned by it, most will die without treatment. Those with only one claw, one eye, two eyes facing each other, six or four feet, hair under the abdomen, bones in the abdomen, stars on the head and back, and spotted feet and red eyes should not be eaten, as they are poisonous and harmful to people." Li Shizhen said: "All crabs are cold and not very poisonous. Mix them with ginger and vinegar, pair them with aged wine, chew on the roe and hold the claws, and taste the flavor slightly. What poison is there? Gluttons eat a lot at once, and they mix in meat and greasy food, eating twice as much as usual. The stomach and intestines are injured, causing abdominal pain, vomiting, and diarrhea, which is bound to happen, and they blame the crabs. What fault do the crabs have?" I think Tao and Li's sayings are enough to increase common sense. Holding crabs after the frost is something we always do, pairing them with wine, yellow or white, each with its own merits. Yellow wine removes the fishy taste, while white wine wards off the cold. Even if we are drunk and full, we are still fine. This is enough to see that the problem really lies in the wine. Most of the wines sold on the market are made with sugar syrup and spirits, while brandy is made with alcohol and ester. There is no need for a reaction. Only those that I make myself are brewed from real fresh grapes, so there is a reaction. Crab roe is very rich in ammonium phosphate, while the meat is rich in potassium phosphate and calcium. Therefore, dead crabs emit an ammonia smell and can turn paint into water. Any lacquerware can be washed with caustic potash or ammonia water to remove the paint. This is clear proof. Because it is a strong alkaline action, it can dissolve glue, paint, and potassium phosphate. When it meets tartaric acid, it can decompose into potassium tartrate and sodium and turn into monomeric phosphorus. The reason why red-headed matches can kill people is the phosphorus poison. Ammonia is ammonia, which is originally a gas, so it causes intestinal rumbling. What Song Yu called "circling the intestines and stirring up the qi" is this state, and the excruciating abdominal pain is caused by caustic potash eroding the stomach wall. If you try it with caustic potash, it will immediately cause burning pain and corrosion when it touches the skin. Potassium, sodium, and ammonia are all neutralized by hydrochloric acid and turned into cough-suppressing and qi-lowering medicine. Taking advantage of rhubarb's one-time purgative effect is like opening the floodgates to release silt, all of which is discharged. The unique feature of rhubarb is that it stops with one purge and does not linger. (Unfinished)

Modern Medicine Journal

First Aid Knowledge Six 191

— Editor

(6) Insect stings and bites

Centipedes and wasps. Their stings are very poisonous. Once bitten, they cause swelling, redness, itching, and pain, which are extremely unbearable. As for the nature of their toxins, medical science has not yet clarified it and remains a question.

For those who have been stung or bitten by insects, quickly apply ammonia water (i.e., dilute ammonium hydroxide) to the wound. It is also advisable to apply cold wet cloths to the swollen and red areas to relieve inflammation and reduce pain.

If ammonia water is not available at the moment, salt or alcohol can be used instead.
