Random Talk

The Issue of Abolishing Corporal Punishment in Elementary Schools 202

— Xing An

The newspaper reports that the Ministry of Education, based on the National Children's Year Implementation Conference, submitted a request to instruct the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to inform local elementary schools' research associations to study the promotion of abolishing corporal punishment in elementary schools and removing all restrictions on children. The original submission and research issues are specially copied and distributed to the education departments and bureaus for compliance.

Corporal punishment was very common in private schools in our country. Most private school teachers had a ruler prepared to beat the palms of students when they could not recite the scriptures, did not answer questions correctly, or committed mistakes. This was the lighter form of corporal punishment. There were also heavier punishments, such as making students kneel on money boards or snail shells. Private schools used corporal punishment with the intention of punishing students, so that they would know to fear punishment, be able to study diligently, and behave according to the rules. Whether this legislation was appropriate and could achieve educational effects is difficult to say. But its cruelty was extremely barbaric. All those who attended private schools as children have a bad impression of the teachers.

Unexpectedly, this kind of corporal punishment is still common in elementary schools today, which is really strange. Today, elementary school students are often beaten by teachers when they cannot answer questions or occasionally make naughty moves. As for more severe punishments, they can still be seen. It is said that this type of punishment is also used in some inland middle schools. Therefore, corporal punishment has become a scheme worthy of discussion in our country's education.

However, corporal punishment is not only practiced in our country's schools, but also in foreign schools. According to Lowes in his book "Are We Civilized?", in the chapter on education, he said: "Until recently, European elementary school teachers often used whips to beat seven-year-old children, causing them to suffer injuries for life. In the seventeenth and eighteenth centuries, young dukes and even kings were brutally beaten by their teachers." Luo Mai's "Theory of Education," in the chapter on punishment, also said: "In the past until very recent times, the punishment of children and young girls was considered natural and generally thought to be necessary in education." But the result made a senior writer feel that his childhood past was not necessarily regrettable. Because after he stopped going to school, he did not have to be afraid of being punished every day, which was the greatest benefit.

Here, we believe that it is inappropriate to use corporal punishment in elementary schools, and it should be abolished. In some respects, corporal punishment may be beneficial to children, but in other respects, it is harmful to children. It will not have any effect on education. Therefore, we strongly agree with the Ministry of Education's instruction to local elementary schools' research associations to study the promotion of abolishing corporal punishment in elementary schools. This year is Children's Year, and we hope that the education authorities can implement the abolition of corporal punishment in elementary schools, relieve children of a layer of suffering, and give children a good impression.

Sleepless Night 203

— Er He

I turned off the lights and lay in bed, but it was difficult to fall asleep. A kind of inexplicable worry invaded my heart. Like gloomy clouds on a rainy day, it weighed heavily on me, making it hard to breathe. My eyes were open, but what was there to see? The top of the mosquito net was blurry, and of course, the outside was also hazy... I was very clear, I knew it was another sleepless night. I straightened my body and stubbornly thought, I was prepared to bear all the troubles of a sleepless person!

So a depressed heart ran wild. Thinking of all kinds of illusory dreams, crimson, orange, gray, purple, black... So immersed in emptiness, I sighed softly, so weakly, like a broken spider silk in the wind. I opened the mosquito net and looked up at the courtyard. The courtyard was lonely. Even the little sparrows that usually broke the silence of the courtyard were no longer noisy at this time. Two old cypress trees stood upright, gloomy and stubborn at the same time. It seemed to be threatening something

Page 22

what. Perhaps this whole courtyard of loneliness was brewed by it? In the silence, I seemed to hear the sound of dew drops touching the tips of the deep autumn grass, I seemed to hear the breathing of the leaves of the old ginkgo tree...

Old ginkgo, I only got to know it when I came here. I often used the attitude of an explorer to explore everything about it. It is particularly majestic, facing each other in the east and west in the courtyard. The one on the east is male, leaning its body and stretching out its old arms. The blue sky at night is particularly blue and particularly high. The male old ginkgo, I know it loves to have absurd dreams, it seems to want to embrace the blue and high sky with all its heart. The female one is more kind, and often ripe seeds fall down with a dull sound because no one picks them, so the fruits are always falling endlessly. The fall of its first fruit was more than half a month ago, but now there are still fruits falling, and perhaps they will not be finished falling in another half a month. Both old ginkgo trees are more than a hundred years old, and their memories are very old. Whenever dusk comes, a bloody red glow is reflected on the branches, and the old ginkgo speaks many old stories in a complicated way. It will say that the red walls of the Confucius Temple have long faded, and after fading, they were painted red again, and the red faded again. It will say that there are charming foxes wagging their tails in the courtyard in the deep night. It will also say that the little sparrows between the rafters do not know how many generations have passed. It knows all the absurd, old, and strange stories clearly, it is a correct history textbook.

Lying on the bed, opening my eyes, quietly listening to the dull sound, I know it is the fruit falling from that female ginkgo tree again. Then a night breeze gently blows, and the leaves flutter down rustling, one sheet, one sheet, I know it is sticking to the grass, or sticking to the soil. Again, a dull sound, a ginkgo fruit falls, again, a dull sound, a ginkgo fruit falls... This sound is particularly loud and clear, shattering the deep dream of the night...

Then the pale moon climbed up from the treetops. The sickly cold light fluttered in through the window, painting a milky white blur on the calligraphy hanging on the wall. Looking carefully, the sparse shadow of the old ginkgo tree is projected on the floor through the window, this is the masterpiece of the autumn night moon, right? The old cypress tree that does not often sway is still suppressing everything with a threatening posture. Four or five sickly chrysanthemums, because they cannot get sunlight, are hiding in a corner of the wall, cowering as if they cannot withstand the slightest sway of the night wind. The little grass is shrinking and waiting for the moistening of the cold-faced and warm-hearted dew drops. As for me, I groped along the edge of the bed, groped along the corner of the table, looked out the window, and looked back at my own thin shadow pressing on the masterpiece of the autumn night moon—the sparse shadow of the old ginkgo tree coming through the window. I almost suspected that I was a terrible ghost!

I don't want to turn on the light, and I don't want to find one or two articles to dispel my loneliness. I am prepared to bear all the troubles of a sleepless person. The night, although it is deep and long, I am prepared for the pale moon to cross the western sky and flutter the sickly cold light in from the west window. I have the stubborn heart of a prisoner about to be executed, I want to see the dawn of the eastern sky.

Lonely Old Age 204

— Xin Ye

One early winter morning, the weather was unexpectedly cold; the gray-yellow sunlight only weakly shone on a flat hillside. Five or six low houses were clustered tightly around the slope, but most of them were already leaning slightly. A curved dirt road stretched out in front of the slope, winding eastward, and could be connected to the main road on Xiaoyao Palace, from which you could go to the town and the lime kiln. A stagnant pool stretched out on the side of the road, and there was also a stone well at the end of the pool; these were to supply the people on the slope with drinking water and washing things. Now half of the water in the pool has been used up, and because it is stagnant water, it has turned dark green. A thin layer of ice is frozen on the surface of the water, but in several places at the "crossing," it has been stirred open by people washing vegetables and rice in the morning. At that time, on the few pine trees floating in the pool, there were several small sparrows leisurely and lively jumping and chirping, some were repairing their wings, and some were turning over the millet in the piles of yellow vegetable leaves by the pool.

Under the old plum tree on the west side, there was a dilapidated Ten Earth Temple. It was sitting there quietly and alone, about ten steps away from those low stone houses. The front of the temple was piled with a row of high and low straw stacks; it was after the autumn harvest of the people on the slope, and they had not yet put the straw into the houses. A mangy thin dog was squatting there biting a dog tick in the sun—

The time was only a moment away from opening at noon; the people on the slope, men and women, had gone to the mountains to collect firewood. Every family's door was tightly closed. The surroundings were so quiet, except for the occasional magpie flying to the roof of someone's house or the old plum tree and calling a few times, the air on the entire hillside was so stuffy that it was like death, and almost no trace of life could be found.

Only the wooden public, who had been forgotten in the Land Temple, was coughing and struggling to get up from the straw bed piled with broken cotton wool in the musty corner of the wall, but somehow. A series of coughs and chokes came from his chest: he felt that his head was swollen badly today, his head was heavy, and his eyelids could not be lifted, the house, the ground, everything was turning in front of his eyes, and even his own person was turning with them. The waist was so painful that it was like someone was breaking it. He closed his eyes and fell back down, but a series of coughs and chokes climbed up from his throat again.

"The frost has fallen, right! The deadly old illness is about to flare up again, flare up... die... it's... also... good..." he muttered to himself, but the ending sound seemed to be with a heavy trembling.

He barely touched the door, and sat down with difficulty on a pile of straw, leaning his body on the straw, looking at the faint and powerless sun. He often spoke so convulsively and laboriously, "Um ya! Um ya!" His face was thin and with a heavy shade, the image of a skeletal skull, with a pair of dry and godless eyes. The clear snot frozen on that clump of gray-white beard was like a row of beads stuck on it, shining. The broken cotton-padded jacket he was wearing had chunks of rotten cotton wool squeezed out of the holes. Sitting in the sun, his body was still shivering! "

He often resented his fate, hoping that he would die sooner, so as to avoid such suffering, but he still did not die, but dragged on like this for another year; this illness came more fiercely in the winter; the wooden public sadly moved his pair of eyes looking at the sun not very vividly, but the bright clear tears stored in his eye sockets seemed to jump out from the tips of his eyelashes.

The sun was crooked to the south, still depressed like an opium ghost's face, only some shadows of the sparse forest had moved a position, but the wind was blowing so hard that the treetops were shaking a little.

Suddenly, the skinny dog lying on another pile of straw stretched lazily, stood up, and dragged its vertical tail to the side of the wooden public. He sniffed at his body very affectionately and lay down gently in front of him. It also seemed to understand the sadness in the wooden public's heart, and gave him a kind of sympathetic comfort...

Soliloquy in a Lonely Building 205

— Shi Weizhi

Autumn

It's autumn, I have the heart of a begonia.

The heart of a begonia is lonely and bleak.

During the day, looking at the green or gray-white clouds, looking at the unchanging chimney, looking at the smoke slowly dissipating from the chimney, this is autumn.

At night, a ten-candlepower light bulb, listening to the rain outside the window, the sound of the rain is like a low complaint and like a cry, besides that, it is a piece of stillness, even the sound of autumn insects is gone, autumn is deep.

Many cigarettes are burned in vain, and many pots of boiled water are drunk in vain, but the heart is still like pale white clouds.

There is no anger, anger can strengthen the will to resist; there is no plan and hope, with a plan and hope, there is the courage to bandage the wounds and fight again; there is only a vast heart like white clouds, there is only a lonely and bleak heart like a begonia.

Summer has passed, winter has not yet come, spring? It's been too long to go, and the days to come are too far away, although I know that spring will inevitably come.

What can I do? Except look at the gray-white clouds, look at the chimney, look at the gradually dissipating smoke.

Or under the ten-candlepower light bulb, listening to a piece of stillness.

Friendship

A friend once said: "A friend is always a friend, and a father is only a relative."

When I read that letter, I saw my friend's anger, I saw my friend's face was red, and he drank a lot of wine.

Sure enough, there was another letter the next day. He advised me to destroy the previous letter.

The reason is: Don't offend friends, this is what I said after drinking,

I destroyed that letter, but I copied that sentence in the manual.

Now, I don't need that manual, I can recite those two sentences:

"A friend is always a friend, and a father is only a relative."

——Friendship, if it is only built on private relationships, then there will always be a day of destruction.

Page 23

Precious Stone Hill 206

— Ai Tu

In the morning, wisps of drizzle hung from the sky, the bleak color spreading vast and wide. Looking out from the window of the small house, the branches and leaves swayed gently. The market of Hangzhou was still so silent, yet such weather was such a disappointment to me! Coming all the way from afar, only to have it drizzle every day! However, because of my excitement, I quickly ran to the street, bought a paper umbrella, and prepared to climb the mountain to play in the rain. At this time, a kind of uneasy adventurous spirit was rising and stirring in my heart. Because I didn't know the mountain roads of Hangzhou, especially on such a desolate and quiet rainy day, which made things somewhat different from the ordinary.

As I ran along the lakeside towards the northwest, gusts of autumn wind brushed against me, penetrating into my chest, and I felt a different kind of coolness. Of course, there were not many tourists at this time, and the calm lake surface was being beaten by the light rain. After running for about twenty minutes, I turned onto the wide mountain road of Baoshi Hill from the back lakeside. From there, I could see the Baochu Pagoda standing on the top of the mountain like a delicate beauty. However, this slanted peak, when viewed from the foot of the mountain, was vaguely half-covered by a desolate thatched cottage and green leaves.

How quiet this road was! On both sides, the black shadows of the jungle swayed, and the rustling sound drifted into my ears. There was no song of birds, and the universe was just a desolate silence. Moreover, the mountain road was so high that a tense feeling arose in my heart, perhaps it could be said to be fear, and I opened my eyes wide to look carefully to the left, right, front, and back. I myself found this infinitely ridiculous. After climbing for a long time, I reached halfway up the mountain, where there was nothing but desolate thatch. It was with great difficulty that I found a small winding path that could be followed. When I entered a dilapidated temple, I only saw the ruined gray walls and the strange drawings and characters that were quietly depicted on them. Climbing up the stone steps one by one, and circling twice in the thatch, I finally reached the side of the Precious Stone Pagoda. At this time, the tense feeling in my heart that had been frightened all along relaxed.

The Precious Stone Pagoda is tall and pointed, different from the ancient pagodas in other places. It is like a graceful beauty, standing proudly on the top of the mountain, overlooking the scenery of Hangzhou, facing the lake like a flat mirror. At this time, the rain had stopped, so I sat by the pagoda, quietly enjoying the happiness of a loner, squinting my eyes, and recalling that the Precious Stone Pagoda, as seen from the lake at night, was hung all over with glittering electric lights, just like a beauty wearing gorgeous and dazzling clothes. Moreover, this pagoda is like a slender and long bamboo shoot. There is an ancient saying, "Leifeng is like an old monk, Baochu is like a beauty." Now, I can see it, especially at night, I can even prove that the saying is true.

In the distance, I gazed at the mountain peaks hidden in the thick mist, faintly. The water waves of the West Lake, shaped like shells, were no different from the bleak sky, spreading out and continuing vastly. The saying "the sky and water merge into one color" is also very true when used to describe the quiet West Lake in autumn. From here, I could also see the North Lonely Hill, which looked like a huge bird spreading its wings and lying in the West Lake. The North Lonely Hill is overgrown with lush green trees, and everything in the mountain cannot be seen clearly. One can only see that it is connected to the lakeside by the Bai Causeway, which is full of willows, and the red wooden Botanical Society Bridge. The Fanghe Pavilion and Xu Xiaoqing's Tomb are arranged side by side on the shore of the back lake, and are only a small shape, just like the broken lotuses on the lake swaying in my eyes piece by piece.

On the quiet Precious Stone Hill, I had enjoyed all the autumn scenery. So, in the desolate wilderness, in the high and dangerous small path of the stone gorge, I hummed a cheerful tune, passed through the Laifeng Pavilion, and went to explore the frightening thatch again.

New Song Introduction 209

Protecting Life Song

(1) Humans are the most intelligent of all things, because humans have human knowledge, human will, and human emotions. We have established human culture and are constantly advancing it; we have expanded human power and thus dominate all living beings.

(2) Humans are the enemy of all things, because humans wield human power, use human weapons, and indulge in human cruelty. For the sake of human enjoyment, we have developed the habit of killing, which has gradually turned into human entertainment, satisfying cruel pleasure.

(3) Please look at the horses and cattle under the whip, with broken skin and rotten flesh; please look at the birds and beasts under the sharp knife, their bones roasted and their oil boiled. Three or five friends use millions of living beings to accompany their meals and drink their wine. Even beneficial insects and birds that are kind to humans are taken and demanded. We have damaged the kindness and generosity in human emotions, cultivated the ruthlessness of mankind, and ultimately led to endless mutual battles between people. It is pitiful that people kill each other until only hills of white bones remain!

(4) Please, everyone, put down your butcher knives immediately and establish benevolence and education; avoid such unbearable abuse, and do not make it difficult to endure. If you can spare them, then spare them. Let hundreds of millions of living beings avoid being destroyed and painfully wiped out. Allow the beneficial insects and birds that are kind to humans to grow and disappear on their own. Cleanse the ferocity and cruelty in human emotions, cultivate the compassion that is the most precious treasure of mankind, and hope that people will never need to use cannons against each other, but only ask that people teach each other to understand that doing good is the highest virtue!

(Epilogue) Compatriots: Do not delay, sincerely cleanse your hearts, know your mistakes and correct them, understand your minds and see your nature, and the truth will never fade. Protecting life is protecting the world, loving things is loving myself!

Comparable to "The Secret History of the English Palace"
